(Jinan) Han Fuju said that the Liu bandits fled northeast from Yiligou, 50 miles north of Juxian, to Guanshuai Meng_ last night. After

Cracks in the American Blue Eagle Movement

The labor unrest in America is currently showing a tendency to spread across various regions, rising and falling incessantly. Whether it be the coal miners in Pennsylvania and Illinois, the automobile factory workers in Detroit, or the silk industry workers in Indianapolis, all have been in constant and fierce conflict with their employers due to demands for higher wages and reduced working hours. On the 6th of this month, six thousand unemployed workers rallied and marched in front of the Minneapolis City Hall, shouting slogans like "We want bread and work," even clashing with the police for several hours. This shows that the brewing labor unrest has become more blatant than the large-scale strike rumors of the steel, automobile, and textile industries in late last month. Such labor unrest has indeed diminished the luster of the Blue Eagle Movement, which was personally promoted by Roosevelt. Some say that Roosevelt's government's major policies may undergo a drastic change because of this, and its impact on the future of the American and global economies cannot be underestimated.

We still remember that when Roosevelt came to power in March of last year, the American financial organization experienced unprecedented panic, thus creating an opportunity for Roosevelt to use dictatorial means. First, he rejected the separatism of the banking system, and then he corrected the laissez-faire habits of industrial and commercial organizations. The reason why he could become the central figure praised by the people was due to the circumstances. When Roosevelt was engaged in the Washington Talks and participated in the London World Economic Conference, his eyes were full of hope, all wanting to achieve the goal of smoothly overcoming the global economic crisis through cooperation. The reason why he could implicitly become the king of the capitalist world was also due to the circumstances. In addition to wielding dictatorship to adapt to domestic and international crises, Roosevelt also felt the need to increase the general purchasing power of society, so he also advocated raising wages and reducing working hours, as if to say that the profit of capital depends on the development of production, the development of production depends on the expansion of the market, and if the market is to be expanded, it will not be successful without increasing the total amount of social income. This is why employers must generously pay the working masses with higher wages. All of this is enough to illustrate that Roosevelt's fundamental plan is only to achieve the goal of accumulating profits by raising wages. However, by doing what he does to get what he wants, workers are bound to resent not getting real benefits, and employers will resist because of their losses, because the current sacrifices, however small, are real benefits, while the future benefits, however large, are still far off and uncertain. Looking at the Roosevelt government's performance in the past year, policies are as numerous as hairs, but their effectiveness is not obvious. The chess game is undecided, only to cause confusion. To this day, not only is it still unable to satisfy the expectations of general capitalists, but also the demands of laborers cannot be met. This is the origin of the surging labor unrest.

However, is the current labor unrest spreading across the country enough to make Roosevelt abandon the policies he has embraced for years? This is still a huge question. According to our observation, Roosevelt is not only unwilling to abandon his existing position, but may even feel the need for dictatorship more strongly. The surging labor unrest will hinder the military-industrial production organization of today and will further impoverish capital profits. In order to implement his policies, Roosevelt will only have to further centralize and monopolize American financial capital before he can talk about maintaining the security of American industry and ensuring profits. From this point of view, is the outbreak of today's labor unrest enough to stop Roosevelt's determination to develop his policies?

Northeast Volunteer Army Determined to Resist Japan; Longing for News from Inside the Pass and Prepared to Kill the Enemy; Li Du's Former Troops Pretend to Surrender to Earn Weapons and Ammunition

Germany Increases Military Spending; Britain Intervenes with the League of Nations; France Also Expresses Unified Action; Germany Says It Does Not Violate the Treaty; Disarmament Steering Committee Reopens Meeting

(London) The British government officially inquired with Berlin about the significance of Germany's move to increase national defense spending, based on the League of Nations' continued authority to supervise Germany. Therefore, the British government can ask the League of Nations to pay attention to any actions that violate the treaty. Britain, France, and other countries have long suspected that Germany has violated the treaty on military equipment. Some sources now say that in view of Germany's new budget, what was done secretly in the past is now being done openly and brazenly. (9th Dispatch)

(Berlin) Germany's increase in national defense spending has caused shock among various countries. Today, an official on Wilhelm Street met with a Reuters interviewer and made a statement to dispel doubts, saying that the army's expenditure of 175 million marks was actually because the army had to be completely reorganized in accordance with the short-term military service system. The navy's expenditure of 50 million marks is intended to be used to gradually refresh old military equipment and old warships. The air force's expenditure of 13.2 million marks is intended to be used to implement public protection plans and reorganize civil aviation affairs, such as replacing single-engine aircraft with multi-engine aircraft and expanding aviation affairs. The increased expenditure does not violate the Treaty of Versailles, because the treaty does not have any binding provisions on military budget proposals.

British Foreign Secretary Simon told the House of Commons today that he had ordered the British ambassador to Berlin to inquire with the German government about this matter. The diplomatic circles in Paris are also paying attention to this matter. It is said that the French government is eager to dispel this doubt but feels that it would be more effective for the British government to negotiate with Germany.

At the same time, the so-called speculation that Britain has a new plan for a disarmament convention is not believed by people in London. It is said that Britain has no new plan, but the British government has not expressed its unwillingness to consider new guarantees for the implementation of the convention. This guarantee is what France wants, namely, sanctions for those who violate the treaty. This kind of sanction is roughly financial and economic in nature.

Disarmament Conference Chairman Henderson has arrived in Geneva. Today, he issued a statement saying that the governments of various countries with whom he has consulted seem to unanimously advocate that there should be considerable guarantees. However, opinions differ significantly on the rigorous implementation of these guarantees. (9th Reuters Dispatch)

(Paris) A certain senior official here claimed today that the former British Ambassador to France, Lord Tyrrell, met with French Foreign Minister Barthou on Saturday and told him that the British government intended to ask the German government to explain whether the increased military expenditure had violated the Treaty of Versailles or was prepared to violate the treaty. Barthou thanked Tyrrell for his report and earnestly requested him to convey to the British government that the French cabinet fully agreed with the British government's actions. (9th Reuters Dispatch)

Disarmament Steering Committee Reopened Meeting Yesterday; Henderson Calls for Facilitating the Convention; British Plan Should be Discussed Immediately

(Geneva) At today's afternoon meeting of the Disarmament Conference Steering Committee, Chairman Henderson spoke, advocating for a slightly longer period of time so that efforts from all sides could lead to the conclusion of an agreement on certain key points. He believed that there was no better strategy than to extend the time limit. He also said that in 1932, even when war was spreading in the Far East, the Disarmament Conference opened with great hope. Unfortunately, this hopeful situation quietly passed, and trust turned into a new competition for armaments. But there is something to be desired, that is, although the military budgets of major countries have now begun to increase, the arms race has not yet been fully exerted. We cannot but admit that the changes in the past few months have made the progress of our work more difficult. He hoped that the participants would not abandon their great cause, because our solemn responsibility is to make the Disarmament Conference achieve a conclusion in accordance with treaty obligations and avoid a new arms race. British representative Eden then spoke, explaining the efforts of the British government to seek an agreement, stating the circumstances of his talks in Paris, Berlin, and Rome. Finally, he said that in addition to other difficulties, there was a fundamental difference between the views of France and Germany. He also said that he did not intend to hinder its progress when exchanging opinions, so he advocated convening a meeting of the Steering Committee on April 30 to discuss the results of the exchange of opinions and decide on the steps to be taken thereafter. Russian representative Stein spoke, advocating for convening a Disarmament Conference as soon as possible and stating the need for countries to conclude non-aggression pacts, adopt Soviet proposals, and determine the definition of aggressor countries. (10th Reuters Dispatch)

(Geneva) Today, according to Disarmament Conference Chairman Henderson, the opinions of various countries on disarmament are not as complex as they used to be and are gradually tending to converge. Henderson's views can be seen in Henderson's review of disarmament negotiations after 1933, which is 32 pages long and will be released at the conference tonight. Tomorrow afternoon at 4:00, the Disarmament Steering Committee will hold a meeting. It is said that the Disarmament Steering Committee to be held tomorrow will decide to convene the Disarmament Conference to be held on May 23 as scheduled. Henderson said, "The differences of opinion among countries on security have gradually dissipated. To this day, all the countries concerned recognize that security must have adequate guarantees. I believe that if countries can negotiate with each other, they will be able to reach a clear provision on security and guarantees, and the importance of this provision will be proportional to the circumstances of violating the Disarmament Convention." US Secretary of State Hull telegraphed from Washington, saying that the United States will still take a non-participating attitude when the future Steering Committee and Disarmament Conference discuss purely European disarmament and politics. US Disarmament Representative Davis is still on vacation, but US Minister to Switzerland Wilson has received instructions from Washington and will be the US observer representative at the Disarmament Conference, but Wilson will not participate in any disarmament discussions. It is said that countries no longer want to propose any suggestions on guarantees and adjudications for punishing those who violate the Disarmament Convention. (7th National Telegram)

British Cabinet Discusses French Note; Preparing to Continue Negotiations

(London) Lord Privy Seal Eden was dispatched to Geneva to participate in the Presidium Committee of the Disarmament Conference. After his departure, the Cabinet Disarmament Committee held a meeting to discuss the French oral note of April 6. According to this document, talks between London and Paris can continue. This is as we initially expected. However, the British Cabinet must wait until the guarantees for the implementation of the Disarmament Convention that France deems necessary have been clearly stipulated before it can consider the new stage of disarmament. However, responsible parties have repeatedly stated to avoid misunderstandings that the British government has always been loyal to the disarmament plan it proposed. It is also said that the issue of German rearmament currently being considered is only the first step in a general disarmament solution. In this regard, Britain has always believed that the British disarmament plan is superior to the Italian plan. Therefore, British personnel are still preparing to conduct negotiations to enrich the guarantees for the implementation of the Disarmament Convention. However, the quantity originally set by the British plan can only be modified within the scope of ensuring that the establishment of the Disarmament Convention can actually reduce armaments. Therefore, the general public formally denied the Daily Mail's claim that Britain will propose a new plan. (9th Havas Telegram)

(London) The Cabinet Disarmament Committee today discussed the French disarmament note, which is quite important. Although the contents of the note have not yet been announced, the outside world has glimpsed its outline, forcing the British government to deliberate at length. The question of whether Britain is willing to guarantee France's security as a condition for France's disarmament is particularly relevant. Some British newspapers believe that Britain's compromise disarmament solution will be based on French suggestions, with the British side limiting economic sanctions to be an obligation in the Disarmament Convention. The News Chronicle reported that if the United States intends to maintain peace in Europe, the United States should not object to accepting economic sanctions. Warsaw The dispute between Poland and Czechoslovakia is generally considered to have ended, but it is still a matter of concern for Polish public opinion. This dispute arose in December of last year, when former Polish veterans held a demonstration in Cieszyn, Silesia, a city on the border between Poland and Czechoslovakia. The two countries had long disputed the city. After a ruling by the Permanent Court of International Justice in The Hague, a protocol was signed in 1925, dividing the city between the two countries. When Polish veterans held a demonstration there in February last year, it caused a stir in both Prague and Warsaw. Three Poles were arrested in Czechoslovakia, and Polish authorities expelled twenty-two Czech residents from Poland. Subsequently, the Czech court ruled to release the three arrested Poles, and therefore it was generally believed that the dispute between the two countries had ended. However, the Clock Newspaper, the official publication of the Polish government with conservative leanings, published a lengthy article today discussing the relationship between Poland and Czechoslovakia, stating that there is a lack of ethnic unity within Czechoslovakia, while Poland has only recovered two-thirds of its territories. The newspaper also stated that Poland's recent signing of non-aggression treaties with Soviet Russia and Germany is sufficient to eliminate the danger of revising Poland's borders. Poland previously shared foreign troubles with Czechoslovakia, but now Poland has nothing to fear. In conclusion, the newspaper expressed much doubt about the friendship between Poland and Czechoslovakia, concluding that the border issue between the two countries, in terms of justice and time, is favorable to Poland. (Havas, 10th) Yugoslavian Capital Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu, en route to Geneva, arrived here at 2:00 PM today, holding a meeting with Foreign Minister Jevtić, and will depart for Geneva in the evening. The meeting between the two Foreign Ministers is of utmost importance, as Titulescu will represent the Little Entente countries in talks with Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov in Geneva, and will also meet with French Foreign Minister Barthou in Paris. After the meeting between the two, officials reiterated that Yugoslavia and Romania have completely identical views. (Havas, 9th)

Prague Foreign Minister Beneš, the General Rapporteur of the Disarmament Conference, has departed for Geneva to attend the Bureau of the Disarmament Conference. Political figures here stated that Beneš will discuss with Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu and Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov in Geneva the issue of the Little Entente countries' de jure recognition of the Soviet Union. It is expected that this matter can be resolved soon, and the Czech government may send an ambassador to Russia by the end of this month. (Havas, 9th)

Japan-Russia War Machine Is Not Mature; Before Japan Concludes a Treaty with the United States, It Will Definitely Not Lightly Launch an Offensive Against Russia—Observation by American Mr. Funn—

(New York) Mr. Funn, who once served as the Far East Manager of the Associated Press, recently published an article in the American Miners' Magazine, stating that Russia and Japan may not be willing to meet on the battlefield. The reasons he cited are divided into five categories. Mr. Funn's paper said that Japan's economic and political ambitions in the Far East indicate that the day of war between Russia and Japan is still far away. And both countries are unwilling to be the first to draw swords. The reasons are as follows: First, the Japanese army has been able to control all of Manchuria; Second, the attitude of the United States; Third, the warlike nature of the Japanese people; Fourth, the war machines of Russia and Japan are not yet mature. He also traced Japan's political and economic conspiracies in Manchukuo after the September 18 Incident in 1931. Japan used the excuse that Chinese people threw bombs on the main line of the South Manchuria Railway on the night of September 18, and then freely began military action to create today's Manchukuo. In his conclusion, Mr. Funn stated that if Soviet Russia attacks Japan, (which no one in the East believes,) then the Soviet Russian leaders must have a full understanding of the burden of war. If Japan attacks Soviet Russia, (a few experienced observers in the East believe that Japan may take this action,) the Japanese leaders must be confident that they can consolidate the power of the Japanese in Manchuria, and also conclude a treaty with the United States, so that Japan's raw materials will be guaranteed to continue. Otherwise, Japan will never launch an offensive against Soviet Russia first. (National News Agency, 9th)

Frequent Disputes on the Chinese Eastern Railway: Transporting Medicines to Russia Considered Illegal; Four Chinese and Russian Employees Detained

(Harbin) Today, several Chinese and Russian employees of the Chinese Eastern Railway were arrested for secretly transporting goods to Russia, causing a great shock. It turns out that Li, the chief medical officer of the Chinese Eastern Railway, Volkov, the chief physician of the Chinese Eastern Railway Hospital, and Galmikov, the director of the hospital's pharmaceutical department, transported a batch of medicines to Russia, and 7,000 rolls of bandages to the eastern section of the Chinese Eastern Railway. The "Manchu" authorities considered this illegal private transportation and arrested them. In addition, Galomov, the chief inspector of the eighth district of Harbin, was also arrested because eighteen freight cars loaded with suspicious goods recently heading to the western section of the Chinese Eastern Railway were missing, presumably having entered Russian territory. (Reuters, 10th)

Labor Unrest in the United States: Auto Workers End Strike; Johnson Meets with Roosevelt; Recovery Administration to Adopt Decentralized System

The auto industry labor unrest in Detroit is becoming increasingly serious. Currently, all small factories that manufacture essential parts for auto assembly have decided to strike. The "Automobile Products Company" is among them. More than a hundred auto factories have had to stop working due to the lack of necessary parts. (Havas, 9th)

5,600 workers manufacturing auto parts in Detroit previously went on strike demanding wage increases. The employers have now agreed to increase wages by 10%, so the strike has ended. In addition, 18,000 workers at the engine manufacturing company, who were laid off due to the parts workers' strike, can now resume work. However, another 18,000 workers who do not belong to the labor union are still continuing to demand a 20% wage increase, but the employers believe that they cannot accept this, so the situation is very tense. There are even rumors that General Johnson, the director of the Economic Recovery Administration, will resign. Although this statement has been denied, General Johnson will submit a plan to President Roosevelt, advocating for the revision of the Economic Recovery Plan, from centralized decision-making back to decentralization, which is indeed the case. (Havas, 10th)

Washington National Recovery Administration Director Johnson suddenly went to Florida today with an assistant to meet President Roosevelt on a yacht. This matter is quite important. It is believed that Johnson will discuss with President Roosevelt new ways to quickly end the labor unrest. McGrath, the labor advisor of the Recovery Administration, is in Detroit, discussing everything with the leaders of the workers of the Motor Products Society and the Airplane Parts Company, who have been on strike since April 6. It is expected that Recovery Administration Director Johnson will order McGrath to investigate the shutdown of the Hudson Motor Company nearby. (Reuters, 9th)

Washington The National Recovery Administration, which was originally solely responsible by Director Johnson, will now be divided into departments to handle affairs and share responsibilities. The Recovery Administration has 400 industry codes and 3,000 employees. Johnson feels that it is necessary for him to only handle the most important events, so he plans to establish a general affairs department, with Mr. Lin Zhi signing industry codes and other documents. (Reuters, 10th)

International Train Derails Near Linz, Austria: 19 Killed and Injured; Rail Spikes Removed; Suspected Political Conspiracy

Vienna The special express train from Vienna to Paris, which departed from Vienna at 11:00 PM last night, derailed between the Horsching and Marchtrenk stations near Linz at 2:30 AM this morning. As a result, two people were killed, five were seriously injured, and twelve were slightly injured. When the train had not yet passed the accident site, a 25-meter-long section of rail had been removed of its spikes and placed diagonally on the side. When the train arrived, it was traveling at high speed, and the locomotive and the first two passenger cars completely overturned, and all other cars also derailed, with only three remaining on the tracks. Most of the victims were railway employees, with only two passengers injured. After investigation, at least seven people would be required to remove the spikes from this section of rail, indicating that this accident must be a conspiracy. However, it is still difficult to understand whether it is a political conspiracy. Linz is the city where the Socialist Party and the Nationalist Party have recently had disturbances, and the location of the train accident has had two previous accidents in 1932 and 1933, both caused by dismissed railway workers. From this, clues can be found. The Railway Administration has offered a reward of 5,000 schillings (Austrian currency) to apprehend the perpetrators. (Havas, 10th)

US Ambassador to Ireland Dies Suddenly at Banquet: Due to Sudden Heart Attack; South Ireland Opposes Land Annuity Issue Being Submitted to Arbitration; Resumption of Negotiations Between Britain and Ireland Remains Distant

Dublin The new US Minister to Southern Ireland, McDowell, suddenly fainted at a banquet tonight and passed away. (Reuters, 9th)

Dublin Tonight, Southern Ireland's Chairman of the Executive Council, de Valera, hosted a banquet at Dublin Castle in his personal capacity for members of the Executive Council and the diplomatic corps. The new US Minister McDowell happened to be sitting next to de Valera. After speeches were given by everyone, the US Minister rose to respond, but his speech was very unclear. He then suddenly fainted in his seat and passed away moments later. It is said that it was due to a sudden heart attack. The US Minister was the manager of several American mines and had served as the Governor of Montana. (Reuters, 9th)

(London) Today in the House of Commons, regarding the dispute between Britain and Ireland, Dominions Secretary Thomas stated that Britain is very willing to resume discussions with the Free State in order to resolve various issues, but the issues must first be recognized as a basis for discussion. The South Ireland land annuity issue is only part of the dispute. The British government has agreed to submit this issue to arbitration, but the Free State does not accept it. Labour MP Grenfell stated that the Southern Ireland Executive Council Chairman and the British Dominions Secretary should find a way to negotiate to resolve the difficulties regarding the arbitration proposal. Thomas replied that he is prepared to meet at any time, but Southern Ireland's de Valera has not yet expressed a willingness to reopen negotiations. Treasury Secretary Betterton stated that Britain collected a total of £2.5 million in special taxes on South Ireland's imports in the past year. (Reuters, 9th)

Water Shortage Panic in Britain: Government to Take Emergency Measures; Private Water Storage to Be Used for Public Use

London Prime Minister MacDonald stated in the House of Commons today that there is a severe shortage of water nationwide and that the government has now decided to take emergency measures to provide relief. Minister of Health Young will introduce a bill tomorrow, the full text of which will be released tonight and will be given a second reading on Thursday. Thames Conservancy Chairman Desborough stated that if this summer is as dry as last year, the water issue will be extremely serious. The amount of water that can be released from Teddington is not 1,400,000,000 gallons, but only 600,000,000 gallons, so the country must have one-third of an inch of rain every three nights to be sufficient for use. The bill to be introduced by the Minister of Health tomorrow will be like an emergency act and will be processed quickly. The bill stipulates that all stored water within a certain period, even on private property, should be made available for public use. (Reuters, 9th)

Hirota Kōki Orders Ariyoshi Akira to Return to Japan by Telegram; Broad Listening to General Situation in China; Hirota Conveys Diplomatic Strategy Towards China in Person

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota officially telegraphed Ambassador to China Ariyoshi Akira today, ordering him to return to Japan. The estimated time of return is about three weeks. Ambassador Ariyoshi plans to return to Japan in late April or early May to attend the conference of diplomats stationed abroad, and report on the general situation in China. Foreign Minister Hirota especially wants to inquire about the negotiations on the issues of through traffic and postal services in North China, the League of Nations technical cooperation issue, the issue of anti-Japanese goods, and the diplomatic situation between China and Britain, the United States, and other countries. Foreign Minister Hirota will also convey the fundamental principles of his diplomacy to Ambassador Ariyoshi in person. (China United Press, 10th)

South Africa's Budget Surplus: Thanks to Soaring Gold Prices

Cape Town South African Finance Minister Havenga presented the budget to the House of Assembly today, containing astonishing figures, which is the impact of rising gold prices. The budget surplus for this fiscal year is £6.5 million, and the estimated surplus for next year is about £3 million. According to Havenga, the gold mining companies have increased their tax contributions, but the dividends in 1933 increased by 51% compared to 1932, and gold production decreased by 545,000 ounces due to the excavation of lower-grade gold mines. (Reuters, 10th)

Indian Government Prepares to Release Political Prisoners: A Gesture of Response to Gandhi

Bombay On April 7, Indian National Congress leader Gandhi advised the people to temporarily suspend civil resistance in order to fight for autonomy. The Indian government believes that Gandhi's move has a great impact on the national situation and feels that it should have a gesture of response, so it will gradually release non-cooperative political prisoners, except for those who have been tried and found guilty of treason. Although the Legislative Bill on the Prevention of Disorders Ordinance may not be repealed for the time being, it will be put on hold and only used when it is necessary to deal with terrorist activities. The order prohibiting the National Congress will also be revoked, and the headquarters of the National Congress and the provincial branches will be allowed to reopen meetings. (Reuters, 10th)

Religious Beliefs Weak in Turkey: Mosques Decrease Year by Year

Istanbul Because Turks are increasingly indifferent to religious beliefs, the authorities have decided to reduce the number of mosques. It is heard that among the 500 mosques, 180 will be closed in June this year, and the monks will be placed in mosques that have not been closed. (National News Agency, 10th)

Ministry of Railways Circular Regarding Holiday Arrangements for Memorial Days

The Ministry of Railways in Nanjing had previously issued a circular in the 19th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1930] to all railway lines regarding holiday arrangements for annual national memorial days. However, following the outbreak of national crisis, orders were received to suspend holidays on various memorial days and months. Now, whenever a memorial day approaches, repeated inquiries are made, causing unnecessary delays. A telegram was sent to the Central Government seeking instructions. Yesterday, a reply was received from the Secretariat of the Central Government stating that regarding the matter of holidays on national memorial days, if the Central Government had previously notified that there would be no holidays, then the original holiday arrangements for national memorial days should be followed. The Ministry has subsequently relayed this instruction to all railway bureaus, committees, and Jiaotong University nationwide for compliance. (10th Special Dispatch)

Overseas Chinese Remittances to China to be Converted to National Currency

The Postal Remittance Bureau of the Ministry of Communications in Nanjing, to facilitate international remittances from overseas Chinese in the Malay Federation of the South Seas Islands and Canada, has agreed with the Malaysian postal authorities that, starting from January of this year, the amount of drafts issued to the provinces of Fujian and Guangdong will be converted to the national currency of China. An agreement has also been reached with Canada that, starting from April 1st, the amount of drafts issued to all provinces of China will be uniformly converted to the national currency of China to reduce losses during remittance. In accordance with the Swedish postal publicity methods, flyers have been prepared and sent to the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission for distribution. The flyers state that the amount of remittances to the Republic of China will be uniformly in the national currency of China. Remitters can know the amount at the time of remittance, and recipients are guaranteed to receive the correct amount of national currency without error. If bank checks are used, sent by regular or registered mail, they are often fraudulently cashed after arrival, which is not as secure as using postal money orders, and avoids various indirect commission fees. (10th Special Dispatch)

Ministry of Communications Orders Investigation into Hubei Ship Accidents

Regarding the drowning of passengers in the accidents involving the "Fuyuan" and "Jingjiang" vessels in Hubei province, the Ministry of Communications in Nanjing has instructed the Wuhan Maritime Affairs Bureau, stating that the "Fuyuan" vessel exceeded the passenger limit, leading to the accident, and should be appropriately punished to prevent future occurrences. The "Jingjiang" vessel is currently being handled by the court, and a resolution should be awaited. Deng Jinshan, the captain of the vessel, did not follow the designated route and acted recklessly, leading to the sinking. He should be prohibited from further service. The bureau is also instructed to order its subordinates to conduct thorough inspections of vessel loading to ensure maritime safety, without being perfunctory or negligent. (10th Special Dispatch)
