Japanese Officers

To Visit North China for Investigation - Large Squadron of Japanese Aircraft Arrives at Malanyu - Negotiations for the Reception of Malanyu Also Halted

According to reliable sources in Beiping, Japanese troops along the Great Wall line have been actively operating again since the 1st of this month. The number of Japanese troops in Saho Bridge and Malanyu within the Xifengkou area has not decreased. Outside Malanyu Town, 29 Japanese aircraft from Shenyang and Changchun flew in on the 4th and 5th of this month, flying low along the Great Wall line every day, causing extreme panic among local residents. Recently, over a hundred retired Japanese officers have been sent to Beiping in succession, residing in the Japanese Embassy. Their mission is to be dispatched to various provinces, including Shanxi, Chahar, Suiyuan, and Shandong, under the guise of traveling, to scout out local conditions. They all carry special missions, which is highly noteworthy. In recent days, Japanese troops in the war zone and at various passes along the Great Wall have also been traveling frequently, appearing quite active. At the same time, the Japanese garrison in Tianjin has also notified our side that they intend to conduct military exercises in the war zone soon, but the date, number of troops, and route have not been specified. Our side will assess the situation before responding. 町尻量基, a military attaché to the Japanese Emperor, was dispatched to China to comfort the troops stationed in North China. He arrived in Beiping from Tianjin a few days ago. At 8:00 AM on the 6th, accompanied by Kikuchi, Chief of Staff of the Japanese garrison in Tianjin, 松尾, a staff officer, and 柴山兼四郎, a military attaché at the Japanese Embassy in Beiping, they departed from Beiping in four cars to visit the Yongjian unit stationed in Gubeikou and inspect the battleground around Nantianmen. They arrived in Gubeikou at 3:00 PM that day. After inspecting the troops, they spent the night at the Yongjian headquarters in Hexi. They left Gubeikou yesterday afternoon and arrived in Beiping at 5:00 PM. 町尻菊池 is scheduled to return to Tianjin by train on the Beining Railway at 8:25 AM this morning (8th) and then travel to Tianjin East for inspection. 柴山 is scheduled to take the train on the Pinghan Railway to Shijiazhuang at 9:00 AM this morning and then travel to Shanxi. Although the Japanese side claims that their mission is to travel, according to investigations, their purpose in going to Shanxi is to investigate the transportation conditions in Shanxi under the instructions of the Japanese Army Ministry, with a particular focus on the development of the Datong-Puzhou Railway. 柴山 is scheduled to stay in Shanxi for a week and then travel to Datong before returning to Beiping via the PingSui Railway. According to sources familiar with the matter, negotiations between Yin Rugeng, the Jiji Administrative Inspector of the Beiping Political Readjustment Committee, and 柴山兼四郎, the military attaché at the Japanese Embassy in Beiping, regarding the handover of Malanyu were underway. Because the Japanese army’s Kamamiya unit with one company of more than 120 troops is stationed in the area, and the Wang Jiren unit of the pseudo-police force is stationed in Dongling, they must both be withdrawn to the north of the Great Wall so that our security forces can take over the defense. 柴山 cabled the Kwantung Army headquarters in Changchun to request instructions. The reply telegram arrived in Beiping yesterday, temporarily postponing the handover of Malanyu. The Japanese Embassy has already notified our authorities. It is rumored that the Japanese side's reason seems to be that the chairman of the Beiping Political Readjustment Committee, Huang Fu, has now left Beiping, and everything will be discussed after Huang returns to Beiping. Therefore, the content is extremely simple. Our side is determined to continue negotiations and has telegraphed Huang to report the standstill and request instructions. Therefore, the issue of receiving Malanyu can only progress after Huang returns to Beiping. (8th)

Northern Route Army Captures Zhaoxie - Now Approaching Ningdu -

A dispatch from Nanchang states that Zhaoxie is located in the southern part of Lean, and is one of the most important bandit strongholds alongside Tengtian in Yongfeng, and Dongpo and Huangpo in Yihuang, no less important than Longgang and Futian. Moreover, Zhaoxie is the throat controlling access from Nanfeng, Yihuang, Lean, and Yongfeng to Ningdu, and is critical to the military operations against the bandits. In 1931, during the joint suppression campaign by the three provinces of Hunan, Guangdong, and Jiangxi, Sun Lianzhong was in charge of the central route and attacked Ningdu head-on from here, suffering great sacrifices before recovering it. Later, due to the betrayal of Dong Zhentang and Ji Zhentong, it was occupied by the bandits again, and has never seen the light of day since. This time, a certain unit of the Northern Route Army attacked and advanced from the south of Lean, defeating the pseudo-model division and the pseudo-guard division, and recovered Zhaoxie on the 5th. The remnants of the bandits fled southeast towards the mountainous areas bordering Ningdu, Guangchang, and Nanfeng. The unit is still pursuing them, and can connect with the national forces at Huangpo in Yihuang and Qia Village in Nanfeng in the east, and coordinate with the national forces that have crossed Shaxi in the west. From here, they can move south to approach Ningdu, and attack the important bandit strongholds of Dajinzhu, Dongshao, Luokou, and Wangpo. The national forces have learned from past mistakes, and this time, they will stabilize each place they recover before gradually advancing. It is expected that they will soon join forces with the three routes of Yihuang, Yongfeng to capture Ningdu. (April 6th)

Large Force of Shandong Army Encircles Liu Bandit - Troops Encircle in Two Layers - Bandits Have No Way to Escape

A dispatch from Jinan states that Liu Guitang's bandit force returned from Jiangsu on the 5th of this month and disturbed Shandong again, running between Yishui, Juxian, Linyi, and Mengyin, hoping to return to their old nest in Mengshan. Han Fuju again sent a large army to track and encircle them. Until last night (7th), the remnants of Liu's bandits fled to the Huangshanpu, Hujiazhuang, Gaozhuang, Zhuchenzhuang, Jiangshan, Longdian, Songlinzhuang, Siqianguanzhuang, Buxizhuang, and Nianzi Zhuang areas, more than 20 li southwest of Yishui County. Because the suppression of banditry was being pursued urgently, they did not dare to stay long and fled southwest overnight. By this morning (8th), the bandit force had reached the mountainous areas of Sijiaoquan Zhuang, Huya, Xiaoyaoling, Lijiaquan, Xiacangzhuang, and Jiangyu, 50 to 60 li southwest of Yishui County. Before noon, most of the bandits were in the Sijiaoquan Zhuang and nearby Yaojiadianzi, Shuiwangzhuang, Xujiayu, and Tianjiayu areas. They once tried to break out to the north from Huya but failed. Most of them then moved to the Xiacangzhuang, Lijiaquan, and Jiangyu areas. Only about one-third of them remained in the Sijiaoquan area.

The area occupied by Liu's bandits is surrounded by mountains on all sides. To the west are Shiniuyu, Zhenjiayu, Shanglizhuang, and Wangjiaanzi; to the north are Yanziyu, Liugongyu, Hutongyu, Cuijiayu, and Huayu; to the northwest are Motiangling, Shangweizhuang, and Xiaweizhuang; to the southwest are Nanqiangyu and Dingjiazhuang; to the south are Tianjiazhuang, Liyanjian, Yangjiaya, Xianglushan, and Majiaya; to the southeast are Yashan and Tangjiahe; to the east is T

Gouhuang Zhuang; to the northeast is Huangshanling. The mountains in the northwest, north, and northwest are very high, with the highest point reaching 450 meters. Only the mountains in the southeast are slightly lower.

The anti-bandit armies actively deployed from last (7th) night until this (8th) morning, and have strictly encircled the bandits on all sides. The west and north sides are surrounded by Sun Tongxuan's unit, the northeast is surrounded by Ning Chunxiao's unit, the east is surrounded by Li Xiangchen's unit, the southeast is surrounded by Li Xuande's unit, the south is surrounded by Ma Guanyi's unit, and the southwest is surrounded by the local militia's Xie Shuxian's unit. The encirclement is divided into two layers. The first layer is only eight or nine li away from the bandits' location, at most ten li. The west, at Zhenjiayu and Shiniuyu, the northwest, at Qiangkuangzi, and the north, at Yanziyu and Heiwang Liugongyu, are Sun Tongxuan's direct troops and Zhang Shulin's brigade. The north and northeast, at Hujia Yu, are Ning Chunxiao's brigade. The east, at Huangzhuang Du Lu Zi, is Li Xiangchen's brigade. The southeast, at Yasha Mountain Xianglushan, is Li Xuande's cavalry regiment. The south, at Yangjiaya Liyanjian, is Ma Guanyi's unit. The east, at Dingjiazhuang and Tianjiazhuang, is Xie Shuxian's unit. Soldiers can see the bandits with binoculars. The second layer is only seven or eight li away from the first layer. The west, at Shanglizhuang and Xiaweizhuang, and the north, at Shangweizhuang Motiangling Huayu Cuijiayu, are all Sun Tongxuan's unit. The northeast, at Huangshanpu, is Ning Chunxiao's unit. The east, at Longshan Guanzhuang Yuanzao Hutong, is Li Xiangchen's brigade. The southeast, at Tangjiahe, is Li Xuande's unit. The south, at Maquanyai, is Ma Guanyi's unit. The southwest, at Nanqiangyu, is Xie Shuxian's unit. Together, they form an oval-shaped large encirclement that is wide at the top and narrow at the bottom. In addition to the two-layer encirclement, heavy troops are deployed at important locations around the perimeter to intercept and strike if the bandits break out. In fact, the bandits have no possibility of escape.

The area surrounded by the army is not very large. The inner layer is no more than 14-15 li, and the east-west is only 17-18 li. Because the army is concerned about the people in the villages occupied by the bandits, it dare not use shelling immediately. Therefore, it adopts a method of gradually advancing inwards, forcing the bandits into the smallest possible area, and then destroying them together. At 10:00 AM today (8th), Liu's bandits attempted to break out north from Sijiaoquan Zhuang Li family Xia Chang Zhuang, taking the Huya path through Yanzi Yu, but were intercepted by Sun Tongxuan's unit. A fierce battle ensued, and the remnants of the bandits retreated to their original locations. Many bandits were killed in this battle, and six machine guns were captured. Li Xuande's cavalry regiment pursued them from behind, capturing six horses and more than 20 guns. It is said that a large number of mortar shells are being transported to the front, preparing to use mortars to bombard the bulk of the bandits after noon today (8th). It is also said that Xie Shuxian's unit and Li Xiangchen's brigade each killed more than 20 bandits and captured more than 10 alive, more than 10 horses, and more than 10 guns while pursuing Liu's bandits yesterday (7th). (8th)

Painful Legal Report on the Far East War

— Paris Correspondence

The Parisian newspaper *Le Journal* on March 79th, carried a dispatch from its special correspondent in Moscow, Mr. Liu Qiane, titled

"The Brewing Far East War," which painfully discusses the relationship between Japan and Russia. It is worthy of our reference, and is specially translated as follows:

A certain Japanese diplomat stationed in Moscow always greets me with a mocking smile. Since the diplomatic relations between the Japanese Empire and the Soviet Socialist Republics have been on the verge of collapse, he has seen me waiting for news from him several times. Although he is extremely cautious, compared to his compatriots who are tight-lipped, he is relatively less inscrutable. Moreover, his English is understandable, and we can talk freely. However, what I am concerned about is his opinion on whether a Japanese-Russian conflict will occur. "We should be vigilant," said General Blücher (i.e., Galen), Commander-in-Chief of the Special Far Eastern Army, shortly before the Communist Party National Congress. "Japan is frantically preparing for war there. It is using a desperate effort to transform northern Manchuria into a fortress, from which it intends to break into our territory." In addition, Kaganovich, the most notable aide to Stalin, who usually speaks for him, also declared before the same congress, "We should prepare to deal with a foreign invasion that could happen at any time." Many foreign observers also feel that a conflict is inevitable, and the only question being discussed is the timing.

This is not the opinion of the person I was talking to. He pointed out to me the scaffolding partially covering the window outside his office. "Look, we are teaching them to repair our embassy, and we are paying for it ourselves." Then his smile became even more cynical. "It is evident that we have no intention of leaving Moscow. There will be no conflict because Soviet Russia is incapable of war. The situation within their country is too serious..."

Let us not pretend to be prophets and first examine the current situation of the Japanese-Russian relationship.

In Moscow, there is no doubt about Japan's invasion plans. What is being strongly emphasized here is Tokyo's territorial annexation intentions at the time of the Russian Revolution. As everyone knows, in 1918, Japan dispatched troops to land in Vladivostok. The internal crisis in Russia allowed Japan to seize the Maritime Province (the area between the Heilongjiang, Ussuri River, and the Pacific Ocean), the northern part of Sakhalin Island (the part of the island south of 50 degrees north latitude has belonged to Japan since the Treaty of Portsmouth in 1905), and Outer Baikal, that is, the area east of Lake Baikal.

In the eyes of the Russians, Japan was preparing for future annexations at that time. Tokyo also supported Admiral Kolchak of the Cossack Navy and Semyonov, who wanted to secede from Moscow and organize an Outer Baikal state, to oppose the Russian Communist Party. At that time, the United States was less interested in truly safeguarding the unity of Russia and more interested in hindering Japan's expansion. Due to the pressure from the United States, Japan withdrew its troops from Baikal in 1920, but it maintained its troops in Vladivostok until 1922.

In 1923, an unfortunate earthquake temporarily weakened Japan's momentum. Japan devoted itself to repairing its wounds. During this new period, its relationship with Soviet Russia improved. Then, in 1925, Tokyo and Moscow signed a treaty. According to the treaty, Japan officially recognized the Soviet government and returned the northern part of Sakhalin Island to the latter. At the same time, Soviet Russia granted Japan the right to mine coal and oil mines in Sakhalin Island, which was necessary for the Japanese fleet's supply depot.

In the years that followed, although the relations between the two countries occasionally experienced minor disputes over the fisheries issue in the Tsushima Strait, they remained fair. However, due to Japan's occupation of Manchuria and the direct threat to Russia's rights in the Far East, the relations between the two countries underwent a worrisome transformation.

From this time on, incidents occurred one after another. The most serious of these was the famous issue of the Chinese Eastern Railway. As everyone knows, the history of this railway dates back to the end of the previous century, when Imperial Russia obtained the right from China to extend the Siberian Railway through Manchuria to Vladivostok. Before the Great War, this was Russia's most powerful tool for gaining a foothold in the Far East. At the same time, Japan operated the "South Manchuria Railway Company." In fact, Manchuria was divided into two spheres of influence: Russia in the north and Japan in the south. The competition between the Russian and Japanese ports of Vladivostok and Dalian occurred simultaneously with the economic division of Manchuria. In 1924, the Soviet government, inheriting the rights of the old Russia and thus enjoying the rights to the Chinese Eastern Railway, signed an agreement stipulating that China and Russia would jointly operate the railway on an equal footing. The management of the railway was shared equally between China and Russia. Since Japan became the master of Manchuria, that joint sovereignty (if we can still call it joint sovereignty) has been transformed from Chinese-Russian to Japanese-Russian. Incidents concerning the railway have occurred one after another, and due to Japan's construction of many new railways, the commercial value of the railway has also been decreasing day by day. Therefore, in May 1933, the Soviet government proposed to Tokyo to sell Russia's rights in the railway to Japan. This was a major concession.

Moscow felt that it did not have enough strength and dared not risk a conflict with Japan. From a historical perspective, such an abandonment resulted in the loss of Russian influence in the Far East. This proposal was ultimately regarded as a confession of Russian weakness. From the perspective of many observers of Russian domestic politics, the severity of the food problem and the dissatisfaction in the countryside forced Soviet Russia to adopt a completely passive approach to foreign affairs. We know that the negotiations for the sale of the railway, which were once suspended in September 1933, are now about to formally resume. There are even rumors that the two sides have reached an agreement on the sale price.

However, the Chinese Eastern Railway issue is only one aspect of the Japanese-Russian antagonism in the Far East. To prepare for a possible conflict and to prevent its two borders from being attacked simultaneously, the Soviet government has been actively engaged in diplomatic activities for the past two years. It has approached France and Germany, and especially achieved the recognition of the United States, which has demonstrated a victory over Japan. Moscow has high hopes for cooperation with Washington. Since this reassuring prospect of cooperation with the United States emerged, the morale of the general public here has obviously risen. The tone of the Moscow press towards Tokyo has become even stronger. The recent speeches made at the Communist Party Congress in January, in addition to advocating the need for war preparedness, also strongly emphasized the various advances that the Red Army's military strength has achieved. Last month, *Izvestia* newspaper said that the Soviet army is the strongest army in the world. It goes without saying that there is some exaggeration in this. Galen, speaking amidst applause at the Communist Party Congress, said, "We have defenses in the Far East. Our borders have been locked down, surrounded by cement and iron. We have our best cadre officers there. We have the tanks and airplanes produced by our First Five-Year Plan." Although Mr. Galen did not mention any specific numbers in public, it is generally estimated that the Special Far Eastern Army has about 150,000 soldiers. In addition, the Soviet Air Force is now one of the strongest air forces in the world. According to the lowest estimate, the Soviet Union currently has 5,000 aircraft of various types. The bombers that hovered over Moscow last May Day can operate within a range of over 1,000 kilometers, which means that carrying 500 kilograms to 1 ton of bombs, these bombers can inflict fatal damage on Japan's major central areas from Vladivostok or any location in the Maritime Province. The Soviet Union now has at least 500 of these bombers, in addition to 1,500 fighters. Its arsenal is all new and is making every effort to manufacture them there. During wartime, the Soviet Union will inevitably encounter extreme difficulties in transportation, which is true. But at the moment, they are striving to rebuild and change the gauge of the Northwest Siberian Railway. Everyone feels that in terms of transportation and military affairs, the future situation may gradually favor the Soviet Union. In addition, although the domestic situation still makes the authorities worry, the unease is less than last year. The recent harvest was very good, although it suffered huge losses due to transportation delays. Finally, in the form of tax exemptions and other benefits, the government has granted many things to the peasants, especially in Northwest Siberia and border areas. Because the Soviet government realized the danger, it has since adopted a more reasonable policy towards the countryside. This does not mean that we can predict the outcome of a possible conflict. Assuming that this conflict is limited to one area (which is probably not allowed by the facts), the comparison of the strengths of the two countries is an extremely complex issue. We dare not make a rash judgment. However, whether a conflict will erupt one day soon or can be avoided through various concessions, one thing is clear: in the end, one of the two enemies must allow the other to act freely in the Far East. Just as Britain, in order to strengthen the defense of India, expanded or tried to expand its influence into neighboring countries such as Persia, Afghanistan, Nistan, Tibet, and Burma, Japan will inevitably strive to invade Mongolia and Outer Baikal in the future to protect the entrance to its abundant colony it has seized, and make the Sea of Japan and the Sea of Okhotsk become a Japanese inland lake. Some people in the Soviet Union even believe that Japan aims to take advantage of China's continued chaos to disintegrate China or unify it under the rule of Puyi. A few days ago, *Izvestia* newspaper said that the Japanese taught Puyi to call himself emperor in order to unite the Chinese under the stale imperial system that Puyi ultimately represents, and at the same time, to call out the danger of communism, so that the world will recognize Japan's hegemony in Asia. Regardless of these hypotheses, we should pay attention to the evolution of this struggle that is developing in various forms in the Pacific Ocean. (Translator's note) Recently, regarding the prediction of the Russo-Japanese War in public opinion circles here, there was an article published by Mr. Poulen in the Paris Review, detailing the distant causes and recent examples of the Russo-Japanese conflict, as well as the reporter's worries about the future. Now there is Liu Qiane's Moscow correspondence in *Le Journal* (March 19), which are all readable articles. After returning from traveling in the Far East, Mr. Poulen repeatedly wrote articles in *Le Temps* and lectured at the Institute of Pacific Relations. He held a fair view on the Sino-Japanese issue, which has won the sympathy of the knowledgeable. Mr. Poulen's observations of China and Japan are consistent with the views of Mrs. Violet Leff, who went to the Far East during the Shanghai War. Mrs. Violet Leff's work on dissecting the current situation in Japan is something that ordinary newspaper reporters cannot do. However, Mr. Poulen was not obscured by the propaganda smokescreen that Japan spent tens of millions of francs on within a few months since the September 18 Incident, and was able to narrate the facts of both China and Japan to the readers nakedly. In particular, he was able to refute one by one the Chinese anarchy and the lack of national organization, which the Japanese side repeatedly slandered and fabricated. He was able to explain in detail the difficulties of China's situation, and was able to point out China's continued efforts in the face of all difficulties, as well as the slight but undeniable good results obtained from these efforts, so that readers can recognize the present and trust the future. This frank and selfless attitude and this courage to hate evil are what we admire. We thank Mr. Poulen because his writings have cleared up many misunderstandings of China by Europeans. We marvel at the boundless power of the Japanese because they have the power to incite arms merchants to interfere, causing many daily newspapers to reject Mr. Poulen's careful articles, making many facts that Mr. Poulen wanted to expose impossible to expose since they discovered that Mr. Poulen's records were detrimental to them. *Le Temps* in Paris published Mr. Poulen's China correspondence "First" on December 22 last year, but until now, there has been no sequel of Second, Third, etc. This is proof. This dispatch by Mr. Liu Qiani introduces Moscow's attitude towards Japan and the situation of the Russian military buildup, some of which we know but not in detail, and some of which we do not know. The last few lines describing Japan's ambitions can further prompt our deep reflection. (World Telegraph Agency)

The Three Provinces Headquarters Expands Its Organizational Content. He and Wu Will Serve as Chief of Staff and Secretary-General Respectively. Six Departments Are Jointly Responsible for Military and Political Affairs. The Troops Transferred South Implement Political Training.

Hankou Correspondence: The General Headquarters for Bandit Suppression in the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui plans to expand into two offices and six departments to unify the guidance of military and political affairs in the three provinces. After several rounds of planning, the organizational method has been completely decided. Under the commander-in-chief and deputy commander-in-chief, there will be a chief of staff and a secretary-general, each with their own office, jointly administering six departments, namely: (1) the General Affairs Department, reorganized from the Adjutant Department; (2) the Military Affairs Department, or Staff Department; (3) the Military Supplies Department, or Logistics Department, under the Chief of Staff. Under the Secretary-General, there will be three departments: (1) the Secretariat; (2) the Political Affairs Department; (3) the Political Training Department. Each department will have a director and a deputy director. This organizational plan has been dispatched by Zhang Xueliang, Qian Dajun, Wu Jiaxiang, and Li Tiancai to Gan, to pay respects to Chairman Chiang for instructions. It is expected to be implemented around the 15th of this month. As for the candidates for each position, it is said that they have been internally determined. The current Chief of Staff Qian Dajun will be transferred to the Nanchang camp to serve as Acting Secretary-General. Liu Chou-peng, the current Secretary-General, will also be transferred. He Zhuguo will succeed as Chief of Staff, and Wu Jiaxiang will succeed as Secretary-General. Tang Guozhen will be the Director of the General Affairs Department, and Ma Zhaoqi will be the Deputy Director. Once Chiang's reply telegram is received and approved, it will be fully announced.

The troops transferred south are all preparing to organize political training departments to implement political training. Li Tiancai will serve as the Deputy Director of the Political Training Department of the Pingjun Branch, stationed in Hankou, and preside over its affairs. In addition, Commander-in-Chief Chiang recently ordered the General Headquarters to instruct all bandit suppression areas in the three provinces to establish public training committees within the jurisdiction command, under the supervision and command of the jurisdiction commander, to handle public organization and training, as well as the protection of earthworks and roads. The members will be the director of the division's political training department, the division leader of the mobile team, the county magistrates of each county, and military personnel designated by the jurisdiction commander. The director of the division's political training department will be the chairman, and the expenses are stipulated as follows: (1) Jurisdiction area within two counties, monthly expenses up to 1,000 yuan; (2) Jurisdiction area within four counties, monthly expenses up to 1,500 yuan; (3) Jurisdiction area within six counties, monthly expenses up to 2,000 yuan. (April 9th)

Remnants of Bandits on the Border of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui Converge and Raid Eastern Hubei. He Zhuguo Dispatches Troops to Defeat Them and Is Currently Pursuing Them. Liu Zhenhua Sets Up an Interest Bureau to Assist the Rural Areas.

Hankou Correspondence: The remnants of bandits from the 25th and 28th pseudo-armies and the 23rd guerrilla force in the border area of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui recently took advantage of the transfer of national troops to jointly raid the area bordering Huangma in eastern Hubei, attempting to break through the defense line of the 57th Army of He Zhuguo in eastern Hubei. Although there are fewer than 3,000 bandits, Wu Huanxian and Xu Haidong, the two bandit leaders, are personally commanding, so the momentum is quite strong. He Zhuguo, stationed in Songbu, immediately dispatched troops to suppress them. There have been two contacts in recent days, and He's troops have defeated the bandits in both instances, capturing many. Currently, the main force of the bandits has fled to Dadong Mountain, and a small force has fled into Shangcheng County in Henan Province. He's troops are currently pursuing them. The 67th Army of Wang Yizhe has also concentrated in Luoshan and Huangchuan, and is coordinating with the troops of Song Tiancai and Liang Guanying to encircle and suppress them. He Zhuguo was originally scheduled to come to Hankou on the 9th to pay respects to Zhang Xueliang, but because he went to Zhongguan Station on that day to inspect the Chang Jingwu Division, and because the spring rain made the road difficult, he changed it to within two or three days. Wang Yizhe will also come to Hankou to pay respects to Zhang after meeting with Liang Guanying in Xinyang. He Zhuguo, newly stationed in eastern Hubei, urgently needs to clarify discipline, so he issued two proclamations, which are recorded as follows: (1) "Since the dispatch of this army, all matters concerning the supply of personnel and horses and public and private supplies must be self-provided and must not be taken from merchants and civilians. All departments have been notified and announced to all in the case. Now that the various troops have successively arrived in Hubei, the following prohibitions must be absolutely observed: (1) At no time is it allowed to forcibly conscript civilians for service; (2) Regardless of the location, military and civilian transactions must be fair buying and selling; (3) All officers must not enter civilian residences without permission; (4) Absolutely prohibit immoral behavior. All of the above items must be strictly observed by all officers and soldiers of this army. If there are unscrupulous people who deliberately violate them, you merchants and civilians are allowed to send them to the army, or file a complaint by name. Once verified, they will be shot on the spot without leniency. In addition to distributing this to all departments, it is urgent to announce it to merchants and civilians so that they are all aware." (2) "This army was previously stationed in various places along the Pinghan Line, and all public and private supplies were purchased by ourselves. There has never been a place to obtain supplies from the local area. Now that this army has been transferred to this place, all matters will still be handled according to the old practice. The supply of personnel and horses is provided by this army, and even the private residences of officers and soldiers are rented at market prices. Even if it is difficult to purchase daily necessities and it is necessary to borrow them locally, the department above the regiment level should issue formal receipts according to the handover procedures. As for the trade of goods, fair trade should be especially fair. Merchants and civilians should not raise prices indiscriminately or disrupt finance. Military personnel should not force sales or interfere with order. If there are unscrupulous military personnel who do not comply with the regulations, merchants and civilians are allowed to send them to the army, or file a complaint by name, and they will be severely punished according to the law. In addition to ordering all departments to comply, it is urgent to announce it to merchants and civilians so that they are all aware."

Liu Zhenhua, Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression in the border area of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, believes that the rural economy in the border area has been completely bankrupted due to the frequent banditry over the years. Now that the remnants of the bandits have been gradually suppressed, the people are returning in increasing numbers, but the fields are barren and they are unable to cultivate them. In order to seek relief, it has been decided to establish an Interest Bureau in the border area, specializing in providing farmers with low-interest loans and the supply of agricultural tools and seeds, so that the returning refugees will not abandon spring plowing. The organizational rules of the bureau have been drafted by the border area headquarters, and the opinions of the three provincial governments have been sought. It can be established within days. (April 9th)

Aircraft Reconnaissance Shows No Trace of Liu's Bandits in Soviet Territory. Wang Jun's Special Train Passes Through Xuzhou and Goes to Bian.

Xuzhou Correspondence: Liu Guitang's bandit troops, between Jiangsu and Shandong, have been repeatedly suppressed by the troops of Wang Jun and Han Fuju. After fleeing back to eastern Shandong, there are currently no traces of bandits in northern Jiangsu. Yesterday (8th), two aircraft from the air force bombing squadron that arrived in Xuzhou flew to eastern Shandong for reconnaissance. There were no traces of bandits in Linyi, Yishui, Ju County, or Tancheng. Wang Jun believed that the bandits had deeply infiltrated into Shandong, and the Shandong army had already dispatched a large part of its forces to suppress them. He then ordered the 7th Division to strictly defend the border of Jiangsu, in order to prevent the bandits from fleeing south again. He then returned to Xuzhou Station by special train from Xinpu this morning (9th) at about 6:00 am. In response to Liu Zhi's telegram invitation, he did not get off the train, but continued west on the original train to Bian. He only summoned Sun Ming, the chief of staff of the staff department, to the train to talk. Wang said, "The remnants of Liu's bandits have mostly fled back to the Aishan Dike area north of Yibei. Our army is strictly defending the line blocking Ganyu and Pixian, Zhu Duji, Chenjia Menlou, Cangshan, Daxu Mountain, Jiagushan, Heilin Town, and other places. The bandits are now more than a hundred miles away from the border of Jiangsu, but the bandits are prone to fleeing, so we must block their path south in advance." Fortunately, the defense was very fast this time when the bandits entered Jiangsu. The villages through which the bandits passed were less damaged because they had not been occupied. Ganyu urban area is currently handling post-disaster affairs, and it is feared that it will be difficult to restore it in the short term. The central aircraft inspected separately yesterday morning. Aircraft No. 65 passed through Pixian, Linyi, Yishui, Ju County, etc., and Aircraft No. 66 passed through Jiagushan, Cangshan, Tancheng, Ganyu, Qingkou, Xinpu, etc. They all returned to Xuzhou in the afternoon and found no trace of bandits. This morning, the Xuzhou detachment leader drove an aircraft to eastern Shandong for inspection and landed in Linyi to meet with a Shandong aircraft. Because the bandits are far away from Xuzhou, it is inconvenient to travel back and forth. They may fly to Jin to assist in the suppression within days. (9th)

Huang Shaohong Visits Taiyuan - Inspecting the Political Situation and Disaster Area Losses -

Taiyuan Correspondence: Minister of Interior Huang Shaohong came to Jin from Ping the night before last. Yesterday (5th), he transferred to the Zhengtai Express train and arrived in Taiyuan at 7:05 pm. Mr. Huang's mission this time is to inspect the various construction projects in Shanxi Province and the disaster area losses. It is reported that he will not stay long and will take the road to Datong after meeting with Yan Xishan, and then go to Suiyuan for inspection, and handle the aftermath of the Sun army. The following is a record of Mr. Huang's arrival in Ping:

Earlier, the Liaison Section of the Pacification Headquarters specifically secured special rooms 17 and 27 and six regular rooms at the Datong Hotel in Taiyuan, preparing them as residences for Mr. Huang and his entourage. Section Chief Xue and Song Zhizheng of the section also went to the station to prepare everything, and the Pacification Headquarters sent a team each of military police and constabulary to the station for security. At that time, many important military and political figures from this province also went to the station to welcome him. After Huang got off the train, he shook hands with the welcomers one by one as a courtesy, and then went to the Shanxi Hotel to rest. The reporter briefly talked with Huang on the journey, asking what other tasks he had besides inspecting the political situation and disaster area losses. Huang replied that there were none, and that he came to Ping to see friends. He also asked if Mr. Yan would be unable to come to Ping in recent days, would he go to the riverside? Huang did not answer, only saying that he planned to stay in Ping for two or three days. After arriving at the Shanxi Hotel, he reminisced with everyone in the hotel's large hall. Zhao Daiwen was the most talkative, and often made the hall laugh. Those who came with Huang included Huang's secretary Shi Chushen, adjutants He Zhiwu and Zhou Jieying, and many others. According to Secretary Shi, Minister Huang's visit to Ping this time is to inspect the politics of Shanxi, stay for two or three days, and then transfer to Suiyuan for inspection, and will return to Beijing from Sui via Ping. That day, Yan Xishan received news of Huang's arrival in Ping and immediately telegraphed the Sui Headquarters to set up a banquet to welcome Huang. At 7:00 pm that night, the banquet was set up in the Sui Headquarters' Zhonghe Zhai. More than 20 important military and political figures from this province, including Zhao Daiwen, Xu Yongchang, Yang Aiyuan, Sun Chu, Zhou Dai, Zhu Shouguang, Li Shengda, Yang Yaofang, Sun Huanlun, Lu Jinli, and Geng Guiting, accompanied him. The conversation was very pleasant. Huang praised the various construction projects in this province. The banquet was dismissed at 9:00 pm. (April 6th)

Jiangxi Ning Tea Exchanged for Polish Goods. The Polish Minister to China Expresses His Welcome. The Provincial Construction Department Requests an Appropriation of 200,000 Yuan for a Pilot Project.

Nanchang Correspondence: The Jiangxi Provincial Construction Department previously planned to exchange Ning tea for Russian oil, but the negotiations failed. It then contacted Poland. It has now received a letter from the Ministry of Industry, stating that the Polish Minister to China has sent a memorandum to the ministry, requesting to exchange Chinese tea for Polish goods, and requested that the memorandum be translated for reference. The Construction Department believes that since Poland has requested to exchange goods for Chinese tea, it is an excellent opportunity to develop the province's Ning tea, and Polish goods are also mostly needed by the province. It should start a pilot project before the province's tea market. Yesterday, it specially drafted a plan and submitted it to the provincial government, requesting a quick appropriation of 200,000 yuan to start the project. (April 9th)

New Regulations for Chaozhou Salt Industry: Abolishing the Abusive Contractor System and Implementing Free Transportation and Sales

Shantou Correspondence: The salt production of Chaozhou has been subject to frequent changes in the system based on the whims of officials. In the past, the salt tax was contracted out, resulting in a sharp decrease in revenue and high salt prices for the people. In coastal salt-producing areas, salt was left to rot on the ground. This year, a new system has been implemented, transforming it into "people's salt, government collection, and merchant transportation." The system divides the area into four major salt districts and establishes warehouses. Coastal salt fields are remeasured, and the salt produced is transported to the warehouses. Merchants then transport the salt from the warehouses to the interior for sale. This measure was announced and implemented on April 1st, abolishing the two contractors, Qiaoshang Dongcheng Company and Qiaoxia Limin Company. The regulations for merchant transportation announced by the Supervisory Bureau are recorded below: (1) Chaoqiao Salt Affairs are divided into Qiaoshang and Qiaoxia. Merchants are allowed to apply for transportation permits and freely transport and sell salt. (2) Merchants who obtain permits must comply with the items specified in the application form issued by the Supervisory Bureau, accurately fill it out, affix the seal of a guarantor store, and submit it for review. Once verified, a transportation permit will be issued, allowing them to declare taxes and obtain licenses for free transportation and sales at any time. (3) Applications from merchants with any of the following circumstances will be rejected: (A) Failure to comply with the items stipulated in the application form or inaccurate filling; (B) The guarantor store is not substantial; (C) Non-national or containing foreign capital; (D) Engaged in salt production or soy sauce business; (E) Previous conviction for salt smuggling; (F) Currently serving in salt affairs agencies. (4) If a licensed carrier violates salt laws or engages in other malpractices, they will be punished according to law, and their permit will be revoked, and their business suspended. (5) Tax rates for Qiaoshang and Qiaoxia: (A) Qiaoshang borrowed and distributed Fujian salt: In addition to paying four jiao (角, tenth of a yuan) of silver dollars per dan (擔, a unit of weight) at Xipu He Li in Fujian, an additional two yuan and one jiao of silver dollars will be levied per dan upon transportation back to Chaoqiao. If distributing salt from Chaozhou salt farms, two yuan and five jiao of silver dollars will be levied per dan. (B) Qiaoxia distributes salt from Chaozhou salt farms, levying one yuan and five jiao of silver dollars per dan. If borrowing and distributing Fujian salt, no deduction will be made, and the salt tax paid in Fujian will also be collected at one yuan and five jiao per dan. (6) All existing surcharges and fees must be paid in accordance with regulations. (Note: These surcharges are numerous, approximately equal to the regular tax.) (7) If tax rates change, all carriers must comply and pay accordingly. (8) If a licensed carrier fails to declare taxes and distribute salt for more than one month, their permit will be revoked. (9) These regulations will take effect on the date of promulgation. At the same time, the Supervisory Bureau announced temporary regulations for cracking down on salt smuggling and regulations for the distribution and sale of salt in various locations. Commissioners have been dispatched to seal up the salt previously monopolized by Limin Company in various districts. Salt merchants in Qiaoxia believe that the heavy surcharges have increased the cost by one yuan per dan compared to when Limin Company handled the monopoly. They are taking a wait-and-see attitude and have not yet applied for licenses to operate. (April 3rd)

Songjiang: Recent Situation of River Dredging

The city river of Songjiang has been silted up for a long time since it was dredged in the 6th and 14th years of the Republic of China. A decision has now been made to dredge it again. In the past, river works were supervised by officials and managed by gentry, utilizing the agricultural off-season to develop water conservancy. According to the report on dredging the Songjiang city river in the 6th year, the east, west, south, and north sections had a total length of nine li (里, a unit of distance) and some odd measures, totaling 16,557 construction feet. The riverbed was deepened by three feet, with a total earth volume of 4,786.13 cubic feet. The cost of the project was 2,799.65 yuan, including difficult excavation and long-distance transportation. The cost per cubic foot was 0.5849 silver dollars, or 0.1785 silver dollars per cubic meter, and 0.5064 silver dollars per cubic yard. Adding water drainage, dam construction, salaries for bureau staff, and miscellaneous expenses, the total was 4,738.40 silver dollars. Even during the river dredging in the 14th year, when rice prices were high, the cost per cubic yard was still less than 0.6 silver dollars, and the total expenditure was less than 10,000 yuan. The current dredging is scheduled to begin after the Qingming Festival. All plans are managed by the technical office of the county government. The proposed budget for the project specifies a total earth volume of 87,256.1 cubic meters, equivalent to 3,0810.13 cubic yards, for the east-west main river. In addition to the earthwork cost of 0.14 silver dollars per cubic meter, equivalent to 0.4 silver dollars per cubic yard, totaling 12,215.85 yuan, there are additional costs for difficult excavation (2,908.54 yuan), long-distance transportation (14,820.55 yuan), and handling fees (2,839.72 yuan), bringing the total project cost to 32,784.66 yuan. This translates to 0.3757 silver dollars per cubic meter and 1.064 silver dollars per cubic yard, a twofold increase compared to previous labor costs. Therefore, the estimated cost of this dredging is no less than 60,000 yuan, several times higher than previous expenditures. However, when soliciting bids, local workers were mostly unclear about the distinction between earthwork cost and project cost, and thus hesitated to participate. No one bid. The three bidders were all non-locals. The winning bid was made by Taichang Gravel Company, which signed a contract with the River Works Bureau, appearing delighted. However, local workers, upon hearing that the project cost was estimated at more than one yuan per cubic yard, were all extremely disappointed.

Frequent Robberies in Fengjing

Tao Xiangqin's family, a farmer in Sizhuang Village, 26th Tu, East Market of Fengjing, was suddenly invaded by more than ten robbers on the evening of the 7th. They were dressed in similar clothes, with their heads wrapped in cloth, and held box cannons. They ransacked the house and escaped with their loot. As they left, Xiangqin's son was shot in the buttocks when he fired a gun. At that time, the villagers heard the alarm bell, but the robbers were not afraid at all. At the same time, three or four other families in the village were robbed, but the amount stolen was not significant. Unsatisfied, the robbers returned to Sizhuang Village on the evening of the next day to rob Tao Xiangqin's house again. Fortunately, Tao Xiangqin had taken his son, who was shot, to Shanghai for treatment and had not returned, thus avoiding the disaster. On the afternoon of the 8th, at Daganghougang outside the North Gate, near the Dazhengtang, when a Shanghai ship passed by, more than ten robbers, armed with guns, ambushed and ordered the ship to stop. The robbers boarded the ship and robbed passengers of cash, clothes, and other items, totaling over a thousand yuan, before fleeing.

Huinan: Prison Director's Inspection Visit to the South

Wang Xinzhi, the Director of the Prison Department of the Ministry of Justice, arrived in the city from Fengxian at 12:00 yesterday morning. After investigating the progress of judicial affairs at the county government, he went to the prison and detention center to inspect the facilities and hygiene with the two judges, Jiang and Wu, and the accompanying technician, Zhou Zhenzuo. He made a thorough examination of the equipment and hygiene and noted that the prison and detention center buildings were not only poorly constructed but also not connected, making security difficult. He proposed converting the buildings and land of the adjacent relief home into a detention center to connect them and instructed the two judges to discuss with County Magistrate Yuan to expedite the implementation of the plan. Wang then left for Chuansha at 3:00 yesterday afternoon.

Haimen: Busting a Drug Trafficking Organization

Wu Yuanyuan, originally from Guangdong, established a drug trafficking organization in Xishi, Jiulong Town, two years ago. Opium was the main commodity, sold in Haimen and Qidong counties. The business was very good, with substantial profits. However, Wu was skilled and had never been caught before. A few days ago, Wu imported a large batch of opium, which was discovered and secretly reported to the Qidong County government. The police were ordered to search the premises and seized twenty-eight packages of opium, and Wu Yuanyuan was taken to the county for investigation.

Ningbo: Careless Factory Fire in the Reformatory

The Huafeng Compassionate Mat Factory, an affiliated workshop within the Yin County Relief Institute Reformatory on Liuting Street, Huxi, in this city, caught fire suddenly at around 8:00 PM on the 7th for unknown reasons. As a result, four flat buildings were destroyed, and one was demolished, with losses estimated at over 1,300 yuan. Furthermore, the raw materials stored by the Huafeng Compassionate Mat Factory, valued at 1,000 yuan, were also completely burned. Fortunately, the military and police effectively suppressed the situation, and no inmates escaped.

Jiashan: Three Pilgrims Trampled to Death

Yu Siguan, Li Changfa, and a young Yang child, farmers from Beidou Tomb, Dingjia Village in this county, hired a boat with other pilgrims to go to the Liuwang Temple in Liansidang for pilgrimage the other day. The temple is very popular, and every year around Qingming Festival, a race is held. Ships from Shanghai and Hangzhou gather, and there are crowds of people. When the welcoming procession reached the Hongqiao of Wangjiangjing, due to the crowds, a disturbance broke out, resulting in eleven people being trampled to death, and twelve others seriously injured. It has been confirmed that Yu Siguan and the other two were also trampled to death.

Salt Smugglers Rob Merchant Ships

Yesterday, several boats of salt smugglers arrived at Qianjingdang, southeast of Fanqing. Each boat carried seven or eight bandits with weapons. They robbed many merchant ships and fishing boats and then fled towards Yaozhuang Bridge with shouts.

Rampant Banditry in the County

On the night before last, over twenty bandits speaking the Jianghuai dialect and carrying wooden-cased guns and Mauser pistols arrived at the homes of Tao Jin and Tao Acheng in Rangxiang Village near Xitang Town in this county. They broke into the house, tied up Tao and his son with hemp ropes, and tortured them to force them to reveal where they had hidden their silver. The two men were covered in injuries, and a significant amount of cash and clothing was stolen. At the same time, the home of farmer Jiang Jinlin in the Eighth District was also robbed by bandits, with losses estimated at seventy or eighty yuan. Although the victims separately reported the incidents to the Public Security Bureau and requested a strict investigation, no arrests have been made to date. With bandits everywhere, it is difficult to sleep peacefully.

Local News

American Silver Investigator Rogers Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday Morning; Rogers States His Mission is Purely Observation, Not Negotiation; Plans to Stay in China for About a Month and Visit Beijing, Tianjin, and Other Places

U.S. President Roosevelt, to investigate the impact of raising silver prices and purchasing power in the Far East, specially appointed Professor Rogers and expert Mr. Burton to come to China on the President Hoover. Mr. Burton disembarked in Japan midway and remained there temporarily for investigation. Rogers arrived in Shanghai on the original ship, arriving at the port at around 9:00 AM yesterday. He plans to stay in China for about a month and visit Nanjing, Tianjin, and other places. Details are as follows:

Welcoming Personnel

Those who went to the ship yesterday to welcome Rogers on the foreign side included Mr. Jaslan, representing U.S. Consul General Cunningham, Commercial Counselor Arnold, and Dr. Young, advisor to the Ministry of Finance. On the Chinese side, Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi sent a telegram of welcome and dispatched Chen Xing, Deputy Governor of the Central Bank, and Xi Demao, General Manager of the Foreign Exchange Bureau of the Central Bank, as representatives to greet him. To avoid misunderstandings, most members of the banking community did not attend, planning to arrange a reception after Rogers' visit.

Arrival Details

The ship was originally scheduled to arrive at the port at around 9:00 PM the night before, but due to fog, it anchored outside the Wusongkou overnight. It entered the port at around 7:00 AM yesterday morning and docked between buoys 11 and 12 on the Yangshupu River at around 8:00 AM. Chinese and foreign welcoming personnel prepared a small customs boat, Jinghui, to greet him. After exchanging greetings with Rogers and others on the ship, they transferred to the small boat and arrived at the new customs wharf at 9:00 AM. Rogers and his party went directly to the Cathay Hotel on the Bund to rest. Accompanying Rogers were his secretaries, Landman and Ichi Arnold.

Rogers' Remarks

Yesterday morning, reporters visited Rogers at the Cathay Hotel and were granted an interview. Rogers first stated that he had departed from San Francisco on the 23rd of last month. While the ship was in Japan, he disembarked in Yokohama and traveled to Kobe, but only briefly, before returning to the original ship for Shanghai. He continued, stating that his mission had been announced by the authorities in Washington. However, it was to observe the international situation and investigate China's silver price problem, without the need for negotiations. He planned to stay in China for about a month and visit major ports such as Beijing and Tianjin to conduct on-site investigations of local economic conditions for reference. Nanjing, as the capital of your country, should be visited first, but the date has not yet been determined. After arriving in Shanghai, he intends to rest briefly and then begin visiting Shanghai bankers and chamber of commerce leaders to solicit their opinions. In addition, he will also visit Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi and Song Ziwen to seek guidance. However, as this is his first visit to China, he is not very familiar with the situation and therefore is unable to express much. He also has no opinions on the silver price issue to express. However, he is well aware that China is a very promising country.

Visit to the American Consulate

After arriving in Shanghai, Rogers did not go out yesterday morning. In the afternoon at 3:00, he met with Dr. Young, advisor to the Ministry of Finance, and talked briefly. At 4:00, Rogers and his secretary, Ichi Arnold, went to the American Consulate on Jiangxi Road to meet and talk with U.S. Consul General Cunningham. Cunningham is scheduled to visit Rogers at the Cathay Hotel today. Rogers is an American silver expert and has served as a professor at Yale University since 1930. During the European War, he served in the U.S. National Guard as a colonel. He is the author of books such as "Stock Trading and Money Market" and "France's Prosperous Progress."

China National Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Guangdong Route: Aircraft Number 16 Missing Yesterday; Only One Japanese Passenger

Shenshi News Agency, Shanghai: Yesterday morning, the weather was poor, with heavy fog. In order to maintain operations, all routes of China National Aviation Corporation (CNAC) operated as scheduled. The Shanghai-Hankou route aircraft took off at 8:30 AM from both locations and arrived at 3:00 PM respectively. The Hankou-Chongqing aircraft departed at 7:30 AM and arrived in Chongqing at 2:30 PM. The Shanghai-Beiping aircraft also arrived at 3:00 PM. However, Sikorsky aircraft number 16 on the Shanghai-Guangdong route went missing after flying out yesterday morning. According to reports, the aircraft departed at 6:00 AM yesterday. Due to heavy fog, which was not conducive to flying, it returned to Longhua at 6:30 AM. It departed again at 8:12 AM. At 8:45 AM, the aircraft still radioed the company, stating that it would fly back due to the weather. However, the aircraft had not returned by 9:00 AM. The company immediately dispatched another aircraft to search along Hangzhou Bay, but the search was unsuccessful due to the heavy fog. At 3:00 PM, the company dispatched another aircraft to search, but the weather along the route was extremely poor, with raging seas and the sky and water blending into one, making it difficult to search from the air. The search was again unsuccessful. As of 7:00 PM yesterday, the exact location of the aircraft was still unknown. CNAC has telegraphed all stations along the route, requesting them to make every effort to locate the aircraft as soon as possible. A Shenshi News Agency reporter learned from the company that there was only one Japanese passenger on the aircraft bound for Guangdong, named Zuemura. The aircraft was piloted by two American pilots.

After the news, the reporter's investigation last night revealed that the aircraft was equipped with the latest engine, the fuselage was stable, and the pilots were very skilled and reliable. There should be no other concerns. It is believed that due to the poor weather yesterday, the aircraft landed at a safe location to avoid danger, and the communication may have been disrupted due to the weather.

New Life Movement

Yesterday's Labor Sector Propaganda: Municipal Federation of Labor Holds a Congress; Over 300 Representatives Attend

Yesterday was the labor sector propaganda day for New Life Movement Week. The Municipal Federation of Labor held a New Life Movement Congress at the Children's Propaganda Corps in Xiaoximen at 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon, gathering representatives from various labor unions. It also dispatched personnel to various labor unions to distribute propaganda materials, post slogans, and supervise workers in carrying out general cleaning and other tasks. The New Life Movement Congress at the Children's Propaganda Corps was attended by Lu Jingshi, a director from the New Life Movement Promotion Association, for guidance. The Municipal Federation of Labor appointed Zhu Xuefan, Zhou Xuexiang, and Ye Xiangdi as the presidium of the congress, Shao Xubai as the recorder, and Long Peiyun as the master of ceremonies. Police officers and boy scouts were present to maintain order. The details of the congress are as follows:

Attending Representatives

The representatives who attended yesterday included Zheng Asan from the Paper Making Union of the Fourth District, Zhu Liantang from the Water and Electricity Union of the Fourth District, Zhou Yong from the Water and Electricity Union, Gu Fuzhang from the Dried Goods Union, Jin Dongting from the Kerosene Union, Ye Xiangdi from the Shipbuilding Wood Industry Union, Hu Zufu from the Soy Sauce Industry Union, Ge Tangting from the Cotton Textile Industry Union of the Fifth District, Xiang Zelin from the Soap and Pharmaceutical Industry Union of the Ninth District, Zhu Xuefan from the Postal Workers' Union, Wang Bingkui from the Wine Making Industry Union, Zhou Xuexiang from the Cigarette Industry Union of the Fourth District, and over 300 others.

Congress Order

The congress order was as follows: (1) All stand at attention; (2) Sing the Party anthem; (3) Pay the highest respects to the Party and national flag and the portrait of the late Premier; (4) The chairman respectfully reads the late Premier's will; (5) Silent tribute; (6) Chairman's report; (7) Speeches; (8) Slogans; (9) Adjournment.

Chairman's Report

After the ceremonial greetings, Chairman Zhu Xuefan gave a report, stating that since Chairman Chiang Kai-shek advocated the New Life Movement in Nanchang, the whole country has responded unanimously. The reason for this is that the meaning of the New Life Movement is to enable the lives of people across the country to be in line with propriety, righteousness, integrity, and a sense of shame, suitable for modern survival, and worthy of being modern citizens, citizens of civilized countries. It also expresses the high knowledge and morality of the people across the country. Therefore, for the New Life Movement, we only need to start from ourselves, start from small things, and if 400 million compatriots can eliminate all bad habits and promote China's inherent good morality and adopt the strengths of the West in clothing, food, housing, and transportation, then the nation will have a day of revival. The labor sector has never lagged behind in various movements, and it is especially easy to implement and effective this time. Therefore, we should make extra efforts for the New Life Movement. Chinese workers, in terms of numbers, account for the majority of the entire nation, and in terms of strength, are also extremely important. Therefore, if workers can first do it conscientiously, it will have a great impact on the entire nation.

Representatives' Speeches

After the chairman's report, Lu Jingshi, a director from the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association, gave a speech, stating that since February 19, when Chairman Chiang Kai-shek gave a detailed report on the New Life Movement at the memorial week in the Nanchang Provisional Headquarters, all parts of the country have attached great importance to it. The so-called New Life Movement is to thoroughly transform the existing corruption, decline, and laxity of the Chinese nation, and create a lively, disciplined, and moral expression in all aspects of the entire nation's life. Therefore, we cannot ignore the New Life Movement because it starts from small things. We must know that the only way to revive the nation is to start from these things. Foreigners have a very agile and lively spirit in researching science and managing industry and commerce, so their material civilization has progressed rapidly. We must emulate this spirit in order to revive the nation.

Aviation News

Huge American Cotton Imports

After the loan-secured American cotton shipment to China was halted, Shanghai merchants and factories have been finding ways to expedite the shipping of American cotton purchased directly. Yesterday, the American ship "Houston City" arrived, carrying 11,750 bales of American machine-spun cotton, worth 1.7 to 1.8 million yuan, which were unloaded at Zhangjiagang. A second batch of American cotton, worth 1 million yuan, is being carried by the "Ville de Lyon" and is expected to arrive in Shanghai on the 26th.

Ships Speed Up Installation of Silver Vaults

Due to the frequent occurrence of pirate ship robberies, Shanghai shipping companies are actively installing anti-theft measures on their ships. In addition to installing iron bars and requiring passenger insurance, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has agreed to add silver vaults to eight of its regular Yangtze River and North and South Seas liners, starting immediately, to facilitate the transport of valuables.

Two Stranded Yangtze River Vessels to be Towed

The Ningbo-Shaoxing Company's "Ningjing" ship, which ran aground on the Dui Feng Reef, has been stranded for five months. The Sanbei Company's "Qingpu" ship, which ran aground on sand in Di Port, has been stranded for half a year. The losses to both ships are over 100,000 yuan each. As the water level is now rising, the Ningbo-Shaoxing and Sanbei companies have dispatched workers and crew to tow the ships. It is expected that they will arrive in Shanghai for major repairs in about a week.

Over Forty Hebei Refugees Transported Back to Their Hometowns by Ship, Free Tickets Issued by Charity Groups, Xinfeng Ship Transporting to Tianjin Today

Last autumn's Yellow River breach caused disasters in various parts of Hebei, and many refugees were left without food or clothing and displaced from their homes. Over forty male and female refugees from the province, including Ge Jingli, fled to Shanghai together, begging along the way. Now that spring has arrived, they urgently want to return to their hometowns, but they lack the travel expenses to do so. Therefore, yesterday morning, they went to the Renji Hall on Yunnan Road and appealed to the Shanghai Charity Groups' Joint Association for Emergency Relief of the Yellow River Flood Disaster, requesting assistance. It is reported that the association has already issued free ship tickets to each of them and has dispatched staff members Ge Yunsun and Chen Hongyou to escort the forty refugees to the South City this morning (11th) to board the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Xinfeng" ship and transport them to Tianjin, where they will be separately sent back to their hometowns.

He has written several books on Far Eastern social issues. Carter previously visited Shanghai three times. He left the United States on January 26th, stayed in Hawaii for two weeks, in Japan for three weeks, and then went to South China and Manila. After touring North China, he will take the Siberian train to Moscow and then go to Germany, France, the Netherlands, England, Canada, and the United States for further investigation before returning to the East.

Electrical Appliance Manufacturing Association Sends Telegram to the Whole Country Urging the Use of Domestic Goods, Foreign Light Bulbs are Actually Made in Shanghai, Same Quality but Higher Price, Those Infatuated with Foreign Goods Can Be Awakened

The Shanghai Electrical Appliance Manufacturing Association sent a telegram to the National Chamber of Commerce and trade associations yesterday, urging the use of domestic electrical appliances. "To all chambers of commerce and electrical appliance associations across the country, the current situation is that rural areas are bankrupt, and all industries are declining to the extreme. Tracing the cause, it is the influx of foreign goods, resulting in countless amounts of money flowing out every year, leading to an economic decline throughout the country. In this environment, we should strive to improve ourselves and vigorously promote domestic goods to make up for the losses and stabilize the livelihoods of the people. However, this matter is of great importance and cannot be accomplished by the efforts of one or two people. It is necessary for the whole country to be united and for production and sales to cooperate in order to achieve results. Before the founding of the Republic of China, our country had few products in the electrical appliance industry, and everything relied on foreigners. Therefore, at that time, the prices of various electrical appliances were surprisingly high. When a domestic electrical appliance factory was established and a certain product was produced, the price of the corresponding foreign product would immediately fall. Over the past twenty years, the number of domestic factories has increased, and domestic electrical appliances have become increasingly complete. Moreover, their quality is not inferior to that of foreign goods, and there is no need for foreign goods at all. The reason why foreign goods can still be active within our country is due to the psychological worship of foreign goods by the Chinese people. What people do not know is that the so-called foreign goods are not made in foreign countries and imported from overseas. In fact, they are manufactured in our country. Taking light bulbs as an example, domestic light bulb factories could only produce long-filament bulbs at first. Later, they were able to produce coiled-coil bulbs, and finally, they were able to manufacture half-watt bulbs. However, there are many types of half-watt bulbs. At first, 155 watts was the highest limit, but now 200, 300, and 500 watts can be manufactured. Their durability is no less than that of foreign goods. All brands of foreign light bulbs are manufactured by one factory in Shanghai. The raw materials and manufacturing methods are exactly the same. The only difference is that the capital is from foreign merchants and not from Chinese. The reason why they do not manufacture in foreign countries and set up factories in our country is solely to avoid our country's tariffs. The Chinese people do not realize that goods sold by foreign companies must be foreign goods, and that foreign goods must be different from domestic goods. Is this not injustice? Moreover, they are the same goods, but foreign goods are more expensive while domestic goods are cheaper. Buying foreign goods is wasting money, while buying domestic goods is self-help. Which is more beneficial to the country and to oneself? Knowledgeable people can tell the difference. Our association is sincerely informing you of what we know. We hope that you will carefully consider it."

Over a Thousand Workers from the Mayar Silk Factory Surrounded the Social Affairs Bureau Yesterday to Petition, The Factory Decided to Close Down, Mediation Was Unsuccessful

New Voice News Agency reports that after the labor-capital dispute over wage reductions at the Mayar Silk Weaving Factory, although Party and government agencies have made every effort to mediate, there has been no result. Yesterday, a large group of workers surrounded the Social Affairs Bureau. Details are as follows:

Mediation Was Unsuccessful

The Social Affairs Bureau had scheduled to continue the mediation committee meeting at 10:00 AM yesterday. The representatives of the workers from the main and branch factories of the factory arrived at the bureau on time, but the capital representatives did not arrive. According to the capital's report on the reasons for non-attendance, the factory has decided to close down. The goal of the mediation meeting convened yesterday was to mediate the issue of wage reductions. Since the factory intends to close down, whether or not wages are reduced is no longer an issue, so there is no need to send representatives to attend. Since the capital representatives did not arrive, yesterday's mediation meeting broke up without any results.

Surrounding the Social Affairs Bureau

The workers from the 7th and 10th factories of the factory, due to the capital stopping food supply, all the workers, starting at 3:00 PM yesterday, went to the downtown area one after another to petition the Social Affairs Bureau. There were over a thousand male and female workers, with female workers being the majority. The purpose of the petition was to demand that the factory maintain the food supply and resolve the issue immediately. After repeated persuasion by Wang Guangqing, the director of the mediation section of the Third Department of the Bureau, the workers were promised that the factory would be responsible for maintaining the food supply, but it was still ineffective. The workers also expressed disbelief in their representatives, becoming more and more leaderless, shouting and clamoring, and the order was greatly disrupted. Although the Public Security Bureau and the Security Team sent police officers to maintain order, they were unable to disperse the crowd due to the large number of people. Until the Bureau was about to close, the workers surrounded the area, lying across the main roads, only allowing people to enter, not allowing people to leave. As a result, the staff of the Education and Health Bureaus were also unable to leave after work. As of the time of this reporter's dispatch, the staff of the three bureaus were still hungry and trapped in the bureau, forming a stalemate. According to the Great Gazette, as of 10:00 PM, the workers had not yet left.

Improved Tea Coloring Material, Tea Industry Colleagues Have Established a Factory to Specialize in Manufacturing, Tea Coloring in the Future Should Use the Factory's Coloring Material, Abolishing the Prohibition and Free Coloring is Definitely Not True

The quantity of our country's green tea sold to North America was originally huge, but later, because the tea shipped was using coloring material, it was banned from import. The great and good market was thus ruined. In recent years, although colored tea can still be imported into Africa and other places, there are restrictions on the use of coloring material. If the quality of the colored tea is not pure, it will be banned from import, which has a significant impact on the foreign trade of tea. At the beginning of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau's implementation of tea inspection, it held an absolute prohibition policy on the export of colored tea. Later, in order to sympathize with the business situation, it specially approved the Ministry of Industry to adopt a gradual elimination method. In addition to stipulating that most places are absolutely not allowed to export, those in Africa and other places can still be shipped for sale within a considerable period of time. However, in order to adapt to the situation in the place of sale, the quality of the coloring material used must be strictly controlled. Last year, special collection of commonly used coloring materials for colored tea was carried out for chemical testing, and it was found that sand green, three fish yellow, etc. are indeed unsanitary for drinking. Therefore, experts researched and invented a variety of improved coloring materials, which were given to local Chinese and foreign tea merchants for trial use, and they all agreed that their effectiveness was indeed better than the old coloring materials. The Shanghai Tea Industry Association has established a factory to manufacture them, and tea merchants in all regions should uniformly use them to avoid being banned from export for using inferior coloring materials. The price of the coloring material is very low. This solution during the transitional era is truly great news for our country's tea industry. The current policy of the Commodity Inspection Bureau is to formulate tea coloring standards on the one hand, gradually reduce the color intensity, and reach the point where no coloring is used at all. On the other hand, it stipulates that the tea coloring should generally use improved coloring materials, and the old and inferior coloring materials should be strictly prohibited. Recently, it was reported that the bureau "reissued an announcement to lift the ban, and since the prohibition has been lifted, it should be possible to color freely according to the old rules," etc. All of these are misreports and are definitely not true.

Article 7: The committee shall have a secretary to handle all affairs. If necessary, a number of staff members may be hired. Article 8: The office of this association is borrowed from the Zhongshan Culture and Education Museum. Article 9: If there are any matters not covered in this by-law, they may be amended by the committee. Article 10: This by-law shall be implemented from the date of its passage.

Director of the News Bureau of the Soviet Embassy in China, Volinsky, Dies

Shanghai, April 10 (TASS) - Volinsky, Director of the News Bureau of the Soviet Embassy in China, died last night (9th) at 11:00 PM. Volinsky had been in Shanghai for less than a month. He was confined to bed due to a heart attack from a chronic illness that had plagued him for many years. Volinsky was born in 1882 and participated in the Russian revolutionary movement very early. In 1903, he was arrested by the Tsarist Russian government and exiled to the Yakutsk region of Eastern Siberia. In the darkest era of Tsarist tyranny, he participated in the historically valuable resistance of political exiles in Yakutsk in 1904. This resistance was triggered by the abuse of the then-governor of Yakutsk Province. As a result, Volinsky was sentenced in 1904 to twelve years of hard labor in Siberia. However, in 1905, he escaped from the famous Alexandrovsk Central Prison in Irkutsk. He crossed the great Siberian forest by ox cart in the winter of that year and finally fled abroad, arriving in London. In London, he served as the secretary of the Furniture Carpenters Association. From 1911 onwards, Volinsky served as a railway surveyor in England, Spain, Africa, Argentina, and Australia. He was the captain of the survey team when new railways were built in Australia, Brazil, and Argentina, with excellent results. After the revolution of 1917, he returned to Russia, worked for the People's Commissariat for Foreign Affairs, and served as the director of the news bureau of the Soviet diplomatic mission in the Baltic countries and Mexico. Volinsky, who was recently appointed to this position, was previously one of the directors of the Moscow Underground Road Construction Project.
