Rickshaw Puller Finds a Large Sum of Money; Returns Home to Become a Wealthy Man; Incident Exposed and Arrest Made After Ten Months

Han Meicen, a native of Hebei, is thirty years old. He previously served as the secretary-general of the 21st Division Headquarters of the Army. On June 20th of last year, he left Nanchang with his wife, Mrs. Niu, for Shanghai. Via Jiujiang and Nanjing, they arrived in Shanghai on the 24th. They then went to Hangzhou for about two weeks, returning to Shanghai from Hangzhou on July 8th. They stayed at the Yipinxiang Hotel for one night and then moved to Room 1, Central Apartments, No. 274 Avenue Joffre in the French Concession. When Han set off from Nanchang, the quartermaster, Du Menghua, gave him a 2,000 yuan draft from the Bank of China, instructing him to purchase raincoats and other military supplies in Shanghai. After Han arrived in Shanghai, he went to the Shanghai branch of the Bank of China and obtained 2,000 yuan in cash (all ten-yuan notes). Together with his own private funds of 1,450 yuan, he placed it all in a yellow briefcase and carried it with him to prevent carelessness. On the evening of July 14th, at about 7 p.m., Han and his wife, Mrs. Niu, left the Central Apartments. They walked to the vicinity of Avenue Foch and Rue de Luzon and hired two rickshaws to visit their friend Fan Shaoxian at No. 33 Xiafei Lane, Avenue Joffre. They put the briefcase on the rickshaw. When the rickshaws arrived at the entrance of Xiafei Lane, Mr. and Mrs. Han got out of the rickshaws, paid the rickshaw pullers two jiao, and went straight into the lane, forgetting the briefcase on the rickshaw. The rickshaw pullers, seeing that the passengers had forgotten the briefcase, did not inform them but instead ran away with the rickshaws. Mr. and Mrs. Han met Fan at his home, talked for about half an hour, and then hired rickshaws to return to the Central Apartments. When they arrived at the intersection of Avenue Foch, Han remembered the briefcase, but he was not sure whether he had taken it with him. He went back to Fan's house and rushed to the Central Apartments to inquire about the whereabouts of the briefcase. The tea room attendant of the apartment, Hu A'er, testified that he had seen the couple leave the apartment with the briefcase. At this point, Han realized that the briefcase had been forgotten on the rickshaw and must have been stolen by the rickshaw pullers. He reported the matter to the French police and asked them to investigate. The head detective dispatched detective Tao Desheng to investigate. Because Han had not identified the numbers of the rickshaws at the time, there was no way to start the investigation. They could only try to investigate carefully. Han lost this large sum of public and private money, and it was difficult to recover the stolen goods. He could only lament his helplessness. Until recently, after ten months, the deputy detective of the French police, Wang Zhihao, received a secret report from an informant that the rickshaw pullers who stole the large sum of money were Ding Kezao (22 years old) and Wang Xuekuan (57 years old), both from Dongtai. They had fled back to their hometown of Dingjia Homestead in Anfeng Town, Dongtai County, and abandoned their rickshaw pulling business, living the life of wealthy men. Detective Wang immediately reported this to the French inspector and requested the Second Special District Court to prepare a document and go to the Dongtai County Government with detective Ma Changxin to report the matter and request the dispatch of police to secretly go to the address to arrest the two criminals, Ding and Wang. On the 2nd of this month, they were transferred to Shanghai, and the next day they were sent to the Second Special District Court for interrogation and detention. Yesterday, Judge Sun Peng, recommended by the judge, went to the Eighth Criminal Court and ordered Ding and Wang to be brought to court for further trial. According to Yuan Jiahuan, the lawyer of the police station, the investigation procedures of the police station in this case were not yet complete, and he requested an extension of seven days to investigate the case and notify the plaintiff to file a lawsuit. The court approved the request and ordered a postponement of the investigation and trial until the 17th. The two defendants were returned to custody separately.

Leaf Open-Hearted's Car Crushes and Kills a Person; Driver Fined Four Hundred Yuan; Compensation Part Transferred to Civil Court

Ye Kaixin, a native of Hunan, who has served as a member of the National Government's Military Affairs Commission, Chairman of the Hunan Provincial Government, Commander of the Fourth Army, and Commander of the 52nd Division, came to Shanghai as a retiree after resigning from his military post, residing at No. 165 Dakang Lane, Seymour Road. He owned a private car with the license plate number 8001 and hired Chen Caihao as the driver. On February 24th of this year, at 2 p.m., Ye went out by car, driven by Chen Caihao. When passing the intersection of Changping Road and Gordon Road, Chen drove carelessly and knocked down a Jiangbei peddler named Wang San, injuring him. Chen did not stop to help but instead accelerated and fled. He was caught by Chinese police officer No. 3233 on duty and taken to the Gordon Road police station. The injured person was sent to Renji Hospital for treatment, but he died on the 28th due to his serious injuries. Because the police did not file a public prosecution, Wang Chen, the wife of the deceased, hired lawyer Sha Xunyi to file a lawsuit against Chen and Ye in the First Special District Court, requesting that Chen be charged with the crimes of Articles 291, Paragraphs 1 and 2, and that Ye be ordered to pay compensation for funeral expenses of 7,200 yuan and coffin expenses of 160 yuan. Yesterday morning, presiding Judge Feng Shide opened the First Criminal Court for the trial. Ye Kaixin did not appear in court and hired lawyer E Sen as his agent. The plaintiff's lawyer attacked Ye's absence, saying that Ye had been summoned by the court and should have appeared in court to be questioned, but he refused to appear, which was contempt of the law. Lawyer E immediately replied that the plaintiff only accused Ye of civil disputes and could be represented by a lawyer according to law. Judge Feng then questioned witness No. 3233, a Chinese police officer, who said that the defendant's car had honked the horn when it was five or six yards away from the deceased, but the deceased did not hear it. The place where he was hit was on the rear wheel fender. The car did not stop at that time. I chased him to the intersection of Binlang Road before I caught him. The court questioned him based on the police record and the prosecutor's autopsy report, which stated that the deceased was hit by the front bumper of the car. Why do you say today that he was hit by the fender? The police officer replied that the record might be wrong. The court immediately said that there was no such coincidence of error and reprimanded him. Then he questioned the defendant Chen Caihao, who claimed that the deceased was careless himself. Finally, the court ruled that Chen Caihao was guilty of causing death due to negligence in his business and fined him 400 yuan. The attached civil lawsuit was transferred to the civil court of this court for trial.

Shanghai South Reduce Rent Promotion Association; Preparatory Meeting Held Yesterday; Decided to Notify All Associations to Join; Declaration Issued to Implement the Initial Intention of Rent Reduction

The Shanghai South District Trade Association's Rent Reduction Promotion Association held its first preparatory meeting at the Nanshi Fisheries Association at 4 p.m. yesterday. Jin Chuxiang, Hong Songjiong, Shao Guoyong, and more than a dozen others attended. It was decided to issue a declaration of the preparatory committee and solicit membership applications. The meeting adjourned at 5:45 p.m. The details are recorded below:

Resolutions Passed

The meeting began with formalities. Chairman Jin Chuxiang reported the resolutions of the previous meeting. Then, the following motions were discussed: (1) The motion to publish a declaration in various newspapers (resolved) to be handled after the date of the general meeting is determined; (2) The motion to notify various trade associations to join this association (resolved) to be passed; (3) The motion to schedule a joint meeting of various trade associations (resolved) to be handled by the Standing Committee on a regular basis; (4) The motion to recommend Hong Song, Jin Chuxiang, and Ye Yunping to draft the association's charter (resolved) to be passed; (5) The motion to send a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting it to notify various trade associations to join this association (resolved) to be handled by the documentation department; (6) The motion to send a letter to the Municipal Council explaining the organization and origins of this association and its willingness to be a backing (resolved) to be passed.

Declaration Issued

The association issued the following declaration: We have heard that the rise and fall of the market depend on the economy as its pivot. Today, the signs of global economic downturn are becoming increasingly profound, and Shanghai, as a major trading port in East Asia, has suffered a setback in commerce since the aftermath of the January 28th Incident. Although the reasons are complex, the tight monetary policy and inflexible turnover are among the major key reasons. Our merchants, in this dangerous environment, are eager to struggle and make efforts, so they are competing to cut prices in order to attract customers. They hope to strengthen their hearts with injections, so that they can survive. However, the purchasing power of the public is already very weak. At first, it was enough to call for a while, but in a blink of an eye, the customers were sparse again. Even if they can continue to sacrifice, it is difficult to maintain for a long time. Therefore, they are overwhelmed and exhausted. The only way out is to declare bankruptcy as a last resort. If this continues, the disaster cannot be saved. Not only is there no hope for the prosperity of Shanghai, but also the collapse is imminent. Thinking of this, it is truly heartbreaking. If there is no way to increase revenue, it is better to retreat and cut spending. This is a definite and unchanging principle in economics. In terms of the current situation, in order to maintain the dying business, the key lies in striving to save expenses. Rent is an important part of the expenses, so the urgent task is to ask for rent reduction. Moreover, the general public is suffering, and living is already difficult day and night. However, the burden of rent, compared to the past, has continued to increase, without stopping. Therefore, the public is eager to reduce rent, just like a severe drought expecting clouds. Observing the general psychology, it is so urgent. Conversely, those who own real estate are not without people with foresight and a deep understanding of justice, and they will definitely be able to understand the meaning of helping each other and automatically reduce their rent. This association, in response to the urgent urging of its members, in order to promote the realization of rent reduction in Shanghai, vows to appeal with a fair attitude and a determined spirit, in order to promote it. We hope that everyone will work together and persist without slackening, and will not stop working until the initial intention is implemented. Then we will see the revival of Shanghai, and this is actually its prelude. This declaration is hereby made.

Raised for Twenty-One Years; Gone and Never to Return; Ge Zhaodi Harboring Other Ambitions; Ge Wenlou, What Can He Bear

Ge Zhaodi, a woman, was originally surnamed Song. She was sent to Ge Wenlou for fostering by her biological mother when she was only eighteen months old, as an adopted daughter. Ge is now fifty-two years old and a native of Qingjiang. He used to work as a mailman for a certain shipping company, earning a meager monthly income, just enough to make ends meet. After raising Zhaodi to adulthood, he sent her to school to study. At the age of fourteen, she was recommended by Ge's relatives to work as a female worker in the Lee Yew Tobacco Company, going out early and returning late, living in peace. Until today, Zhaodi is twenty-one years old, and suddenly on December 29th of last year, she left and never returned. Ge Wenlou was deeply afraid that something unexpected might happen on the way, so he reported it to the Fourth District, First Sub-District of the Public Security Bureau and asked them to investigate. Unexpectedly, on January 8th of this year, Ge Zhaodi suddenly hired lawyer Yin Jinghao to publish a statement in the newspaper, declaring that she would restore her surname to Song and sever the adoptive relationship with Ge Wenlou, as well as terminate the engagement with Shen Xiaomao's son, Xinfa. The content roughly stated that Zhaodi was raised by Ge, but since Ge married a second wife and gave birth to his own daughter, he had different intentions and did not treat Zhaodi as his own daughter. Moreover, the engagement with Shen Xiaomao's son, Xinfa, was arranged by Ge's wife, and never obtained her consent. Although she had repeatedly expressed her opposition, it was ultimately ineffective. She had no choice but to go out and make a living on her own. Zhaodi is now an adult and has the right to autonomy. Therefore, she publishes this statement to sever ties with Ge and terminate the relationship between adoptive parents, and notifies the Shen family to terminate the wrongly arranged engagement. At the same time, lawyer Yin sent a letter to Ge Wenlou, and Ge realized that Zhaodi had harbored other ambitions and did not want to return. Twenty years of nurturing and hard work were in vain. What can he bear? He hired lawyer Zhu Sifei to file a petition with the Mediation Court of the First Special District Court, requesting to live together, but it was unsuccessful. He then formally filed a lawsuit, but Zhaodi's address was unknown, and he requested a public announcement for service. Yesterday morning, Judge Luo Chongtai presided over a hearing in the Seventh Civil Court and ordered a public announcement for service.

Unmarried Husband Unwilling to Marry Ugly Woman; Adopted Daughter Drinks Poison in Grief; Farm Girl Unable to Avoid Pity; Zhang Hesheng Is Too Cruel

Du Jinbao, a woman from Pudong, is twenty-one years old. Her father, Xiang Tao, is a farmer in the countryside. When she was young, her father betrothed her to her cousin Hesheng (who runs the Shixingguan Restaurant at No. 100 Hengfeng Road, Zhabei)'s son, Honggen, to be his wife. Three years ago, she was adopted into the Zhang family. Unexpectedly, Honggen saw that his fiancée was not very beautiful and firmly refused to marry her, practicing marriage autonomy. Therefore, although his father planned to choose an auspicious day on the second day of the eighth lunar month of last year to consummate their marriage, he always opposed it and it was difficult to achieve. Having no other choice, Honggen suddenly ran away from home, and there has been no news of him since. The woman missed him day and night and was filled with depression. A few days ago, thinking about him, she felt hopeless and wept silently, feeling more and more resentful. She suddenly had the thought of being tired of the world. She secretly swallowed opium to commit suicide. Later, her father-in-law caught a glimpse of her and immediately sent her to Guangren Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective. She then died. The hospital reported to the Xinza Police Station and ordered detectives to investigate. They then carried the body to the Fielun Road autopsy station. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Local Court appointed Prosecutor Diao Chengtang, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi, to go to the station to examine the body. After examining the body, they questioned Zhang Hesheng, who recounted the previous situation. Mr. Diao then announced that the deceased, Du Jinbao, was a woman, and she died from opium poisoning. The body was handed over to Zhang Hesheng to take back for coffin burial.

Car and Freight Car Collide Violently; Tragic Deaths and Injuries; Yin Wenming and His Wife Injured, Son Dies; Laborer Yang Shengjin's Legs Also Broken

The Ford Motor Company's No. 12543 on assignment, carrying passengers Yin Wenming and his family of three, was traveling near the Bund Customs. A No. 17015 freight car of Zhengtai Coal Company was driving ahead. The Ford car suddenly collided with the rear of the freight car. The driver could not brake in time, and the front wheel of the Ford car crashed into the abdomen of the car, damaging the axle and wheel hub beyond repair. The long footboard of the freight car also protruded straight into the window of the Ford car. Passenger Yin Wenming and his wife, Bao, suffered head injuries. Their son, named Fenfang, suffered a concussion and died shortly afterward. The legs of the small worker Yang Shengjin on the Zhengtai freight car were also broken. Later, the police officers on duty arrived at the scene to record the car numbers and sent the injured to Renji Hospital for treatment.

Joking Causes Death; One Slap Leads to Anger; Sharp Knife Enters Directly and Breaks Abdomen

Wang Youchun, a native of Changzhou, is thirty-seven years old and makes a living selling fruit. He and his fellow townsman, Xu Yingen, live in the same courtyard house at No. 15 Yuanheli, Laobeimen. The second landlord is Cai Tianlai, who is also from the same town. On the morning of the 8th of this month, Wang and Xu went out together to sell sugar cane. When they walked to the entrance of the alley, they started with jokes, and then a verbal argument broke out. Then they fought each other fiercely. Wang Youchun slapped Xu in the face. Xu was furious and stabbed Wang in the abdomen with a sharp knife used to peel sugar cane. The knife pierced the intestines, and even pulled them out. The abdomen broke open, blood flowed everywhere, and he fell to the ground. The second landlord, Cai Tianlai, reported the matter to the First Sub-District of the Second District and arrested Xu. He also sent Wang to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, the injury was in a very dangerous condition, so he died on the afternoon of the 9th. The chief of the police station interrogated Xu Yingen, who confessed that they were joking with each other, and Wang Youchun became angry and slapped him in the face. He used a knife to scare him for fun, but unexpectedly hit a vital part. He was at a loss and pulled it out quickly, causing the abdomen to break open. He asked for forgiveness, etc. The case involved human life, and it was submitted to the Third Section of the Public Security Bureau for investigation. He also ordered Jiang Pingyang, the head of the Ninth Ward, to report to the local court for examination. Yang An, the prosecutor, was appointed to the scene for inspection. He ordered the family members to collect the body for burial, pending the arrest of the murderer for investigation.

Ministries of Finance and Industry; Draft Relief Measures for the Silk Industry; Executive Yuan Orders Shanghai Municipal Government, etc. to Handle; Municipal Party Department Notifies Silk Workers' Union

The Fourth District Silk Workers' Union of this city, because the silk industry of this city is depressed, the factory cannot maintain, and workers are unemployed, which is very worrying, therefore, they separately telegraphed to the municipal government and the central government to request relief. It is heard that the municipal party department has received a letter from the Central Secretariat, which has ordered the Ministries of Finance and Industry to draft four relief measures. The Executive Yuan considers it feasible and orders the Shanghai Municipal Government, the Ministry of Railways, the Ministry of Communications, and the Economic Commission to handle them. The first item is "Exempting all local silkworm cocoon and factory silk donations and taxes", which should be considered for reduction or exemption by the Shanghai Municipal Government. The second item is "Reducing the freight for mulberry seedlings and silkworm cocoons", which should be earnestly verified and reduced by the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Communications. The third item is "Expeditiously establishing a silk industry control committee", which should be verified by the National Economic Commission. The fourth item is "Providing relief by the Shanghai Municipal Government first taking loans and planning loans or issuing public bonds", which should be properly planned and handled by the Shanghai Municipal Government. It is now known that the Economic Commission has replied to the Executive Yuan, and the Silkworm and Silk Improvement Committee of the association has been organized and established. All plans concerning the improvement of the silk industry, reduction of costs, and improvement of trade methods have been started by the association for overall planning. After the Municipal Party Department approved the notice from the Central Government, it has transferred the previous situation to the Fourth District Silk Workers' Union for notification.

Failure of Chinese Cigarette Industry's Request for Funds from the Ministry of Finance; Tax Bureau Responds that Proposal Must Come from Cigarette Business Committee

The Chinese Cigarette Industry Association previously requested government funding for relief due to poor business and inferior tobacco leaves. The Ministry of Finance agreed to allocate 300,000 foreign dollars, designating the funds specifically for improving business operations and tobacco leaf quality. However, the Ministry declined to approve the Association's proposed construction of a clubhouse, citing its limited local benefit. The following is the text of the Tax Bureau's letter to the Association: "Regarding your previous letter concerning the cigarette fund allocation, which was discussed at the Third Annual General Meeting where it was decided that the funds should be managed by the Association and used for assisting in anti-smuggling efforts, improving tobacco leaves, and constructing a clubhouse, and requesting approval and prompt allocation of the funds, this matter is under review. We received a letter from the British American Tobacco Company stating that the Ministry of Finance has allocated 300,000 yuan for improving the cigarette business and requesting that Chinese companies have the right to propose ideas for the use of these funds. This Bureau submitted the case to the Minister for approval, and it was determined that the 300,000 yuan is allocated for the entire cigarette industry to improve business operations or quality. The anti-smuggling assistance and tobacco leaf improvement proposed by the Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Industry Association at its annual meeting are consistent with the original approved plan to improve the cigarette business. However, the construction of a clubhouse is a matter for the Association itself, only benefiting a portion of Shanghai cigarette factories, and was not included in the original plan. Therefore, it cannot be included in this use. Furthermore, this Bureau previously formed a Cigarette Business Committee consisting of Chinese and foreign cigarette merchants to research and reorganize the cigarette business, and requested the Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Association to convene Chinese and foreign cigarette merchants to establish the committee. These Chinese and foreign cigarette merchants have legitimate opinions on the use and distribution of the aforementioned funds and can directly propose them to the Business Committee. After a decision is made and approved by the Bureau and submitted for approval, the funds can be disbursed. This will eliminate disagreements and boundaries. You should comply with this process. In addition to sending a separate letter to the British American Tobacco Company, we are sending this letter to the Shanghai Chinese Cigarette Industry Association for your information and compliance. Sincerely, the Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance."

Jiang Feng Airplane Transported to Shanghai; Dismantled, Arrived Yesterday, and Entered Factory for Repairs; Repair Costs Estimated at Over 1,000 Yuan; Repairs Expected to Be Completed in One Month

The Jiang Feng seaplane, self-manufactured by the Naval Aircraft Manufacturing Department, crashed. The Navy dispatched the Chu Tai warship to the site of the crash in Leqing County, where craftsmen from the Department, including Lin Guotian, dismantled the plane and transported it to Shanghai. The plane arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday afternoon. It is reported that yesterday afternoon at 3 PM, the Department Director Zeng Yi-jing and engineer Wang Chong-hong conducted a second inspection and ordered the craftsmen to unload the plane and bring it to the Department's factory for repairs. A reporter from the Min Yan News Agency visited the Department yesterday and was told by Mr. Wang that the float of the Jiang Feng plane was completely damaged, one wing was lost, and the fuselage was completely shattered. However, the engine is still in good condition and can be used. The estimated repair cost is over 1,000 yuan, and the repairs are expected to be completed in one month. It is also reported that aviation instructor Xu Chengqi is being treated at the Red Cross Hospital for a fractured rib and is expected to recover in one week.

Maritime Affairs Bureau: Meeting Minutes of Ship Collision Conference

The Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau's Ship Collision Dispute Resolution Committee held its tenth committee meeting at 2 PM yesterday. Attendees included Peng Hu, Director of the Maritime Affairs Bureau, Sha Huijia of the Pilot's Association, Xu Zufan, President of the Merchant Marine School, Chen Ganqing of the Marine Insurance Association, He Daoyun, Section Chief of the Second Section of the Maritime Affairs Bureau, and Zhang Zhuzun, Head of the Examination Division. Chen Baoyan attended as an observer. Peng Hu was elected as chairman. The resolutions are as follows: (1) Regarding the collision between the An Tong Steamship Company's Da Xing ship and the Tai Ping Steamship Company's Xin Ping ship at the Wusongkou, the Committee's ninth meeting determined that the Da Xing ship should be held liable for the collision. The An Tong Steamship Company requested a retrial. The decision: the company's statements and the Customs report did not prove that Da Xing was being pursued, so the request for a retrial should not be considered. (2) Regarding the San Bei Company's Heng Shan ship sinking the Ding Sheng steamboat, the captain of the Ding Sheng reported the collision. Because the Heng Shan ship sailed on the ninth, no one came to answer questions. This case will be discussed again at the next meeting. (3) Regarding the collision between the Chuan Shan Company's Chuan Shan ship and the Jin Chang Sen sailboat outside of the Shipu port in Zhejiang, the captain of the Chuan Shan ship, Cai Yechang, and the first mate, Xin Xinchang, testified about the collision. Because the Jin Chang Sen was being repaired in Fuzhou, no one came to answer questions, so no judgment was made.

Hong Li Ship Escapes Danger After Rescue

A sudden storm and heavy rain in Changde, Hunan, caused merchant ships to be stranded, but the San Bei Company's Hong Li ship escaped danger by retreating into the water during the storm and heavy rain. The strangeness of the event is unparalleled. The details are as follows:

Hong Li Aground

The Hong Li ship of the San Bei Company's Changsha line, ran aground near Xiani Port in Changsha at the end of last month due to shallow water. Multiple rescue attempts failed to tow it away. The Changsha Customs, considering it an obstruction to navigation, sent personnel to join the Changsha San Bei Branch to assist in the rescue, but it was still difficult to pull it out. The cargo was unloaded, and the rescue was postponed until the water rose again. Unexpectedly, a strong wind recently occurred, affecting the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. A storm and heavy rain occurred in the Xiang River, and the Hong Li ship was battered by the storm. The ship was pushed into the waterway in the middle of the bank, and the ship was safe.

Yu Hang to the Rescue

The owner of the Hong Li ship urgently requested the Changsha branch to send a ship from Shashi to rescue it to avoid losing the opportunity. When the Hong Li ran aground, the Xiang River water level was 4 feet 7 inches. After the storm, the river water sharply decreased to 4 feet and continued to decrease daily. The Shashi branch ordered the Yu Hang ship to fly to the location to rescue it. Yesterday, the San Bei Company received a telegram stating that the Hong Li ship had been rescued from the dangerous shoal by the Yu Hang ship and is now planning to sail empty to the Changsha riverbank to dock and inspect the ship for damage in preparation for repairs.

Establishment of the China Patriotic Progressive Association

The China Patriotic Progressive Association's declaration states, "In this autumn of international turmoil, all countries in the world are urgently expanding their military capabilities, uniting their nations, striving for progress, and working hard to become stronger in order to preserve their existing situation and national survival in the Second World War. The military-national education and arms race of Germany, Italy, Japan, and Russia have made astonishing progress. The future crisis is imminent. Looking back at our country since the September 18th Incident in the Northeast, we have suffered humiliation from strong neighbors, the impact of natural and man-made disasters, political chaos, rural bankruptcy, backward thinking of the people, and the decline of the aspirations of young people. The fate of the nation is in urgent need of salvation. However, corrupt elements are using religion to amass wealth, and the ignorant people are being deceived, believing that fortune and misfortune are determined by divine beings. This has become a widespread practice in all walks of life, and the spirit of the people has declined to this extreme. Young people are the future masters of the country. Young people in all countries are honing their physical and mental abilities to become the backbone of the future nation. However, most of our country's young people are arrogant, listless, and pursue vanity and entertainment. National demise and extinction are imminent. Seeing this crisis, the members of this association are shuddering with fear. Based on the principle that every citizen is responsible for the rise and fall of the nation, we gathered patriotic comrades on March 20th in Shanghai to establish the China Patriotic Progressive Association. Our purpose is to correct people's hearts, eliminate superstition, promote martial arts, and promote the inherent spirit of the nation. We have no partisan affiliation. We hope that all our compatriots at home and abroad will support us and provide guidance to correct our shortcomings. We humbly ask for your consideration."

Shanghai Municipal Council Public Health Department Undertakes Massive Rat Control Campaign

The Shanghai Municipal Council Public Health Department believes that rats not only damage clothing but also transmit diseases, which is detrimental to public health. Therefore, it has manufactured tens of thousands of wooden rat traps and hired workers wearing yellow uniforms with black letters (PHD) on their backs to place them in shops and homes in various areas of the concession in order to capture rats and reduce the spread of disease. The captured dead rats will be soaked in chemicals and buried in the ground.

Establishment of the Dongmen Road Rent Reduction Association

Various businesses on Dongmen Road in the Nanshi district organized a Rent Reduction Association Nanshi District Branch, which held its inaugural meeting at the Water Industry Association at 10 AM yesterday. Attendees included all businesses on Dongmen Road and representatives from the Ice and Fresh Fish Industry Association, Fruit and Local Goods Industry Association, Box Industry Association, Shoe Industry Association, and Nanshi Goods Industry Association. Representatives from the Rent Reduction Association Nanshi District Branch were present to guide the meeting, including Mr. Shen Xin-fu. Over 200 people attended. Chen Yong-nian (Qing Sheng Box Shop), Xu Jian-sheng (Manager of Xie Yuan Fruit Shop), and Ying Jiu-xiang (Manager of Wu Zhou Pharmacy) were elected as temporary chairpersons. The chairpersons reported the purpose of the meeting, and District Branch Representative Shen Xin-fu delivered a speech. Eleven executive committee members were elected on the spot: Zhu Han-wu, Yao Xiang, Wang Ming-gang, Hu Zhi-tong, Huang Guang-zu, Jiang Gui-chun, Mao Xu-cheng, Chen Yong-nian, Xu Run-sheng, Ying Jiu-xiang, and Xu Xian-chang. The resolutions are as follows: (1) The association will be named the Shanghai Rent Reduction Association Nanshi District Dongmen Road Branch. (2) The association's charter was approved. (3) The association's address will be temporarily located at the Fruit Association at 1 Dongmen Road. (4) The first executive committee meeting will be held on the 12th of this month, where three standing committee members will be elected. (5) Before the rent reduction is resolved, rent will be paid at 70% of the original amount. If the landlord refuses to accept it, the tenants will voluntarily deposit it in the bank. (6) The Nanshi District Branch will be notified for record-keeping. (7) As an incidental motion, each tenant will voluntarily assume all expenses of the association, approximately 5 yuan per building, to facilitate the process. The meeting adjourned after the resolutions were passed.

Ye Zhongfang's Wife Sues for Divorce

Lu Shuang, from Suzhou, was previously appointed by the National Government as Consul in Kobe, Korea. He returned from his travels a few years ago and focused on business. Lu's daughter, Lu Yinglan, 26 years old, married Ye Zhongfang (nickname "Little Jitterbug"), the eldest grandson of the late Ningbo businessman Ye Chengzhong, who was living in Shanghai. Ye, who possessed a large fortune, spent his days indulging in alcohol and frequenting dance halls. In November of last year, he took a dancer, Lu Xiaomei, as a concubine and then abused his wife, Lu Yinglan, in every way. Therefore, Lu, who lived at the Shanghai Villa on Huanlong Road, hired lawyer Dong Banggan to file a petition with the Second Special Court's Mediation Division for mediation of a divorce and an order for alimony. Because Ye had moved and his address was unknown, the case could not be served, and the mediation failed. Therefore, a formal lawsuit was filed, stating that since the plaintiff's marriage, she had been repeatedly abused by the defendant. She had been beaten in the past and had filed a lawsuit in the French Court. Recently, the defendant had sold all of the plaintiff's dowry and clothing. The defendant was romantic and had taken dancer Lu Xueli as a concubine before taking dancer Lu Xiaomei as a concubine in November of last year, which led to the plaintiff's abuse and adultery. The family's happiness has been completely lost. The plaintiff is unable to continue living with the defendant and requests that a divorce be granted and that she be compensated for losses and alimony of 100,000 yuan. Yesterday morning, a summons was issued, and only the plaintiff and her lawyer, Mr. Dong, were present. The defendant was still unable to be served and did not appear in court. The judge tentatively scheduled a new date for the summons and adjourned the court.

Lost and Found Leather Bag: Commendable Integrity of a Shanghai Public Bus Inspector

Longhua is one of Shanghai's famous scenic spots. During the bright spring when peach and plum trees are blooming, tourists are as numerous as clouds and never-ending. Especially on holidays, it is even more lively. Longhua Road is almost like the Shanyin Road. Last Sunday (the 8th), a gentleman took his family to visit Longhua. After the visit, they boarded a public bus of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities to return home. Because the passengers were extremely crowded, there was barely room to stand. The gentleman's family inadvertently left their leather bag on the bus in a hurry. The bus inspector found it and submitted it to the management office for safekeeping. The office then sent a letter to the gentleman based on the name and address filled in on the park ticket in the leather bag, asking him to find a guarantor and come to claim it in person. When he claimed it, he checked the items and found that nothing was missing, and the amount of silver dollars was more than double what he remembered. All items were handed over. He offered a reward, but it was firmly refused. When asked for the inspector's name, he refused to tell. The gentleman was overjoyed to have found his lost item, and the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities and the inspector's conscientious work are exemplary for modern civil servants.

Tragedy of Life Under Oppression: Wife Becomes Prostitute and Husband Acts as Lookout for Income; Repeatedly Arrested and Punished

Min Luorui, 35 years old, from Jiangxi, and his wife Liu Xiuying, 25 years old, reside at No. 7 Yuqing Lane, West New Bridge Street, French Concession. Min has been unemployed recently and ordered his wife to work as a prostitute to earn a living. Every night when Liu goes out to solicit customers in the street, Min follows her to watch out and prevent her from being arrested by detectives. On the 7th of this month, at about 1 AM, Liu was soliciting customers at the intersection of Moulin Street on Avenue Edward VII when she was spotted by detective Xu Wensheng, who stepped forward to arrest her. Min immediately rushed forward to obstruct the arrest. The detective arrested Min for obstructing official business. It was discovered that Liu Xiuying had been arrested 21 times for soliciting customers as an unlicensed prostitute from June of last year to the 2nd of this month, which was truly detestable. The next day, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court. The police lawyer, Yuan Jiahuang, explained the case, prosecuting them under Article 142 and 248 of the Criminal Code and Article 43, Section 3, of the Police Regulations for obstructing official business, offending public morals, and prostitution. Under questioning, Liu admitted that she was a prostitute last year but has stopped now. Min denied obstructing the detective's arrest. After reviewing the confession, Judge Qiu found Liu Xiuying guilty of violating the regulations and sentenced her to a fine of 5 yuan as a warning. Min Luorui was returned to custody and will be interrogated on the 12th after further investigation.

Fire at the Entrance of Dongmen Road: Fire Breaks Out in the Upstairs Warehouse of the Funan Cigarette Company

Yesterday at 6:05 PM, a fire suddenly broke out for unknown reasons in the warehouse on the third floor of the Funan Cigarette Exchange Shop at the entrance of Dongmen Road in the Nanshi district. Flames quickly spread and broke through the roof. Upon hearing the news, the Firefighting Association immediately sounded the alarm. Fire trucks from various districts rushed to the scene to connect water and extinguish the fire. The fire was eventually extinguished. Only a small room in the shop's warehouse was burned. The contents of the room were mainly matches, empty cigarette boxes, and soap boxes, so the loss was minimal. However, while the fire was raging, all vehicles traveling through the area and the No. 2 circular route and No. 1 streetcars of the China Merchants' Electric Tramway Company were unable to pass because the fire trucks and hoses were placed across the road, causing a complete traffic blockage. Traffic was restored after the fire was extinguished half an hour later. Afterwards, the police officer from the area took Shen Cailiang, a clerk from the shop, to the district headquarters for preliminary interrogation. Shen said that the shop owner was Weng Bingyao, from Ningbo, and that the small warehouse on the third floor was insured for approximately 5,000 taels. He said that he did not know the cause of the fire. Because the matter involved a fire, the police will secretly investigate the truth about the fire and detain Shen temporarily. Weng Bingyao will be arrested and sent to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Liu Wenkui, 26 years old, from Haimen, works at the Chinese Underwear Factory in Jinsitu Temple in Western Shanghai. The interior is meticulously equipped, fully filled with cold and dry air. Once fur garments enter, they are isolated from the outside world and can be permanently nourished in suitable cold and dry air, keeping their colors unchanged forever and prolonging their lifespan. Based on the principle of serving the public, the fees are particularly low, approximately a few jiao per item. For such a low price, fur garments can be properly stored, avoiding damage and theft, and can also be borrowed to facilitate economic turnover. Therefore, in recent days, important figures from the party and government and prominent figures in the business community have entrusted their furs for storage, and business is booming.

Correspondence: On the Status of Accountants as Impartial Persons, Not Witnesses

The accountant system in our country has been in place for only a little over a decade, and social observation has not yet fully understood it. It is often mistakenly regarded as a purely witness. Government offices sometimes have doubts about adding a commitment letter to the report. Therefore, there are examples of explanations.

Regarding accountants, the current regulations include 25 articles of the "Accountant Regulations" promulgated and implemented on January 25th of the 19th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1930], 8 articles of the "Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Accountant Regulations" promulgated and implemented on September 11th of the 19th year, 12 articles of the "Accountant Review Rules" promulgated and implemented on February 18th of the 19th year, 6 chapters and 29 articles of the "Accountant Service Rules" promulgated and implemented on May 3rd of the 17th year [of the Republic of China, i.e., 1928], and 22 articles of the "Organizational Charter of the Accountant Disciplinary Committee" promulgated and implemented on December 3rd of the 19th year. All are recorded in the "Complete Collection of Current Laws and Regulations of the Republic of China" recently published by the Commercial Press. The responsibilities, status, and authority of accountants, as well as the procedures for performing duties, the types of documents to be prepared, the standards of conduct, the treatment by punitive government offices, and the regulations of uniforms, are all clearly listed in detail. If you read through them, you will have no doubts. However, since there are many national laws and regulations, it is not possible for everyone to be familiar with them. Sometimes, overlooking the examination or simply inferring based on assumptions can lead to great errors, losing the original truth. It can differ based on location, vary based on the person, have different views before and after, or suddenly arise from occasional doubts. In recent years, government offices and accountants in various places have experienced countless feelings of being unable to comply due to these doubts. Accountant associations in various places have often proposed discussions on such issues to the National Accountants Association, and accountants in various places have also frequently inquired about these issues to the Shanghai Accountants Association. Observing the main reason for their doubts, most of them mistakenly believe that the status of accountants is that of a purely witness. Because of their misunderstanding of the status, the responsibilities, authority, procedures, and formalities of performing duties are all involved in suspicion. Whether it is government offices, social stakeholders, or parties involved, they often have this kind of seemingly correct but incorrect doubt about accountants. Even accountants themselves, due to environmental reasons, may sometimes have to abandon their original clear understanding and long-standing conventions and reluctantly cope with the urgency of the environment. If this continues for a long time, they may unknowingly create a track that is not in accordance with legal principles, or even infer different tracks based on their own assumptions, which is not the original intention of the country to create an accountant system and provide social effectiveness.

According to the above-mentioned regulations, the status of an accountant is that of a purely impartial person, not a witness, which is already clearly indicated. A witness only proves the truth of the facts at the time. If the facts are like this, they say it is like this; if the facts are like that, they say it is like that, without the need for identification. Therefore, once a word is spoken, it cannot be changed, like dyeing white with black. Those who speak the truth are witnesses. Fearing falsehoods, they are disciplined by law and intimidated by commitment letters. However, the auditing of accounts by accountants, whether it is an audit report or an appraisal of accounts, is all based on their academic knowledge and theories to make an impartial judgment. Academic knowledge cannot guarantee that there will be no negligence, and theories cannot prevent new innovations. Scholars throughout the ages have researched one meaning without end, and some have written hundreds of millions of words without being able to make a decision. How can this be disciplined by law or intimidated by commitment letters? Therefore, it is said that accountants are purely in the position of impartial persons, not witnesses.

For example, judges rely on legal principles to adjudicate. Legal principles are the same, but opinions may differ. Legal provisions are the same, but their adoption may differ. Academic knowledge has omissions, and theories differ. Therefore, there is a three-trial system for litigation, and it is not necessary to blame the judges of the first and second trials. Auditing of accounts has an example of re-examination, but there is no regulation that the original auditing accountant should be held accountable. If accountants are regarded as fixed witnesses of society, are judges also fixed witnesses who must provide commitment letters? For example, doctors also rely on medical skills and theories to diagnose diseases, but their examination and judgment cannot guarantee that there will be no differences in theories, nor can they be disciplined by law or intimidated by commitment letters.

Article 24 of the "Accountant Service Rules" stipulates that if there are doubts about the matters reviewed and appraised by accountants, another accountant may be entrusted to re-examine or re-appraise them. It also states that if the re-examination or re-appraisal is different from the original examination or appraisal, the court may be requested to send the documents issued by the two accountants to the accountant association, which shall prepare an impartial written statement in accordance with Article 13 of these rules and submit it to the court. Firstly, there may be doubts. Secondly, there may be re-examination and re-appraisal. Thirdly, if there are differences between the two, it is clearly indicated that accountants use academic knowledge for appraisal and cannot guarantee that there will be no negligence, just as judges' judgments rely on legal principles but cannot guarantee that they are all correct, and doctors' diagnoses rely on medical theories but cannot guarantee that they are all the same. How can a commitment letter forcibly restrict them? This academic and theoretical judgment is purely from the perspective of scholars, standing in the position of impartial persons, without any involvement of witnesses, and there is no reason to provide a commitment letter.

Some may doubt that accountants' auditing and appraisal cannot avoid differences in theories and omissions in academic knowledge, so what is the value of the accountant's report? If what you say is true, the accountant's report seems insignificant. Then how can we give society a sense of trust? I do not know that accountants bear the heavy responsibility of impartiality. Even a few words or phrases carry great responsibility, and that responsibility is only the word "impartial." Omissions in academic knowledge refer to the power of identification. Differences in theoretical knowledge refer to different results of argumentation. However, the truth of the matter does not shake because of this, and the responsibility for impartiality does not disappear because of this. It is clear that the accountant's vocation is impartiality, and the accountant's position is purely that of an impartial person, who will never tarnish their vocation or lose their effectiveness because of omissions in academic knowledge or differences in theoretical knowledge.

Then, does the responsibility for impartiality also need to be guaranteed by a commitment letter? There is no legal principle in the world for impartial persons to provide commitment letters. Those who bear the responsibility for impartiality do not need legal sanctions. According to the above-mentioned accountant regulations, all accountants should be subject to the close supervision of the competent head office and the supervisory authorities in various locations. There are strict disciplinary laws, and there are clear name registration. Although it is not necessary to provide a commitment letter in each case, the seriousness is actually greater than providing a commitment letter in each case. If it is necessary to guarantee credibility by providing a commitment letter in each case, then officials must also take an oath for each matter in addition to swearing to take office. Moreover, the matters entrusted to accountants do not necessarily all belong to the government. Those that belong to the government can provide commitment letters to the government, but for those that are privately entrusted for auditing and appraisal, to whom should the commitment letter be provided? If it is necessary to ensure impartiality and then bear responsibility by providing a commitment letter, then accountants can only be exclusively appointed by the government to be a kind of civil servant and cannot serve the general society. This principle is clear without further explanation.

As for today's conventions, as I said before, I dare not guarantee that they are all the same. However, examining myself, since I have been performing the duties of an accountant, I have not provided a commitment letter in any of the audit and appraisal reports, and the government office has not held me accountable for providing a commitment letter. However, there are times when there are differences in the treatment of impartial persons and witnesses, and in the treatment of notification letters and subpoenas. There are even times when the same case is regarded as an impartial person and sometimes as a witness, sometimes a notification letter is used, and sometimes a subpoena is used. Sometimes, in the capacity of a witness, in addition to inquiring about things, which seems like giving testimony, the accountant's duties are also involved, or the explanation of accounts is also involved. Furthermore, examining various places and accountants, they may not all be the same. This is what is called differing based on location, varying based on the person, having different views before and after, or suddenly arising from occasional doubts. The accountant system has not been established for a long time, and all the regulations have not been widely understood by society, so there is inevitably a state of confusion.

Now, because Lawyer Huang Chui has inquired the Shanghai Accountants Association about whether it is customary to add a commitment letter to the accountant's audit and appraisal, I have given this explanation. My foolish knowledge dares to correct it before my fellow accountants and sages in the world.

Reading Q&A

Another Example of Studying International Issues (1)

Reading Guidance...

This is my second time communicating with you, please forgive me for not writing any more tedious greetings.

The international situation is changing rapidly, truly making it unpredictable. Like the fact that Japan and the United States cannot share common interests in the Far East, this is a current reality that everyone knows. Moreover, there are many international affairs commentators who have said that Japan and the United States will inevitably have a war in the Pacific, and the only question is the timing.

At that time, when I read their arguments, I also felt that they "made sense." But who knew that Japan and the United States would not only not go to war at present, but recently there has even been talk of a compromise exchange of notes. Several international affairs commentators must be breaking out in a cold sweat upon hearing this news! Because ironclad facts have overturned their conclusions. However, clever international affairs commentators will never admit defeat. They cleverly say that the economic relationship between England and the United States is even more serious than that between Japan and the United States. Therefore, if Japan can have a considerable understanding of the United States and allow the United States to get a share of the pie in the Far East, there may be a possibility of a compromise between the United States and Japan to deceive us. Therefore, I have recently become suspicious of these contradictory remarks. They can use a skillful pen to sway opinions, but we cannot blindly follow them for a long time. However, how can this problem be solved? I must ask for your guidance!

(Letter from Zhao Linxiang)

We have also previously presented an article on studying international issues, and then briefly discussed some principles of application in "How to Study the Northeast Problem." Recently, it is probably due to the tension in the international situation. In the reader's letters, quite a few people can apply the methods we have previously proposed to practical problems. Naturally, this is a sign of progress and is very encouraging.

Mr. Zhao Linxiang is commendable for being able to pay attention to the remarks of general commentators in this change in Japanese-American diplomacy and make comparisons before and after. We also find it not surprising that Mr. Zhao is deeply dissatisfied with their remarks because their arguments appear correct on the surface but have shortcomings. Because their use of the "observation method" is too formalized, too mechanized, and cannot examine the growth, change, and influence on the current situation of the forces of various aspects of the relationship together, processing this extremely complex and intricate relationship layer by layer and adding it to the central core of analysis. It is not impossible to take the opposition between Japan and the United States in the Pacific as the center of the analysis for studying the relationship between Japan and the United States, but what is manifested in Japanese-American diplomacy is not only a reflection of this opposition; it is more complex than this. Naturally, when studying the relationship between England and the United States, we should not forget that England and the United States stand at the main opposing poles in the capitalist system, but the reflection of the relationship between England and the United States in foreign texts is not to put on a stern face every day and shout for war. Furthermore, we should also pay attention to the fact that the relationship between Country A and Country B is not as simple as the relationship between Zhang San and Li Si, because Country A or Country B is itself a synthesis of contradictions. There are changes in class forces within a country, and there are changes in the forces of various groups within a class (referring to the bourgeoisie). For example, industrial capitalists are opposed to financial capitalists, and industrial capitalists are also opposed to agricultural capitalists. Therefore, in politics, there is the opposition of various political parties with the above-mentioned powerful people as the background (the reason for these many conflicts of interest is very simple, but it would be too lengthy to explain the reasons in detail. If readers want to study, they can send a letter explaining, and this department will answer in another letter.) These changes in forces will naturally affect a country's external economic and political combat power, which is the so-called external national policy. This national policy is a unit of international power synthesized from many contradictions, which in turn constitutes this great synthesis of international contradictions. (To be continued)

Our Country's Track and Field and Basketball Preliminary Selections for the Far Eastern Games

Athletes from Various Places Come to Shanghai One After Another

A Group of Athletes from North China Arrived in Shanghai This Morning

The Preliminary Selections Will Be Held This Saturday and Sunday

Our country's preliminary selections for various events to participate in the Far Eastern Games are about to be held. It has long been decided that football and swimming will be held in Hong Kong. Track and field and basketball will be selected in Shanghai on the 14th and 15th of this month. Men's volleyball will not have separate preliminary selections. Although it has been decided that the Wang sisters from Shanxi will participate in women's tennis, it is said that the Huang sisters from Beiping have more skilled tennis skills and may surpass the Wang sisters from Shanxi, so there will be a preliminary selection competition, which is still unknown. The baseball team will arbitrarily select a team from North China, Shanghai, Guangdong, Hong Kong, and other places. The National Sports Association is currently busy preparing everything. The details are recorded below.

Athletes from Various Places Depart One After Another

The Track and Field and Basketball Teams from North China Arrived in Shanghai This Morning

A group of 30 track and field and basketball athletes from North China, led by Zhao Wenxuan, took an ordinary train south from Tianjin on the 9th and are scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 7:00 AM this morning. Mr. John Ma arrived in Shanghai yesterday and is busy contacting the Sports Association about everything. The athletes from North China are staying at the YMCA on Sichuan Road, which has been arranged, with a lodging fee of 50 cents per person per day. The team includes 12 basketball athletes and 16 track and field athletes, all of whom have hopes of attending the Far Eastern Games. A group of 17 track and field and basketball athletes from Nanjing, led by Zhang Dongping, will take a train to Shanghai from Nanjing tomorrow. Lin Shaozhou, a famous high jumper from Fujian, led by Chen Zhang'e, is scheduled to arrive by plane tomorrow. Furthermore, the Hubei basketball team will arrive in Shanghai on the Jianguo ship on the evening of the 10th, including 9 team members and one coach.

North China's Basketball Strength is Very Strong

Qiu Zongcheng of the Jinan Public Security Bureau Came to Shanghai at His Own Expense

(Jinan Electric) Today, 29 athletes from North China participating in the Far Eastern preliminary selection, led by Dong Shouyi, departed for Shanghai to participate in the preliminary selection. Dong said that the basketball strength this time is stronger than that of the previous Far Eastern Games, and the track and field results are also very good. Furthermore, Qiu Zongcheng of the Public Security Bureau Security Team came to Shanghai at his own expense to participate in the 1500-meter and 800-meter Far Eastern preliminary selection.

The Sports Association is Busy Preparing for the Preliminary Selection

The Active Basketball Court is Gradually Completed

The National Sports Association is currently preparing everything, such as hiring staff and coaches to go to the Philippines, judges for the national preliminary selection, and selection committee members. The track and field field is being renovated. Because the basketball room was destroyed by fire, an active floor is specially installed in front of the special grandstand of the baseball field, which has been completed and is currently being painted. Electric lights and basketball hoops are being rushed to be installed within days, but the weather is not good, and the work is greatly affected.

Four Teams Participate in the Basketball Preliminary Selection

Four People from Shanghai Participate in the Swimming Preliminary Selection

The registration deadline for the track and field, basketball, and swimming preliminary selections was yesterday. There are four basketball teams: North China, Nanjing, Shanghai, and Hubei. For swimming, Shanghai has Yang Yuanhua, Zhu Jiongpei, Li Rixin, and Li Mingyang, and Wuchang has Zeng Qingshe. Hong Kong and Guangdong have the most people, but the list is unknown. More than 60 people participated in the track and field competition, with Shanghai having the most, as it is closer to home. Even if the results do not meet the standards, those who are not far off can be accommodated to join. The track and field list is listed below.
